Refuting Taklif al-Muhal: The Obligation of Abu Jahl
Hanafi response to Ash'ari objection on taklif al-muhal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between general (ijmali) and specific (tafsili) belief obligations to refute the claim that Allah obligated the impossible for Abu Jahl.

Core Idea
Believing the Prophet does not require believing the report of your own disbelief.

The Ash'ari school argued that Allah's obligation on Abu Jahl to believe the Prophet included believing the Prophet's news that he would not believe—a self-contradiction and thus impossible. The Hanafi response is nuanced: the obligation covers only the general articles of faith, not the specific news about Abu Jahl's fate. This lesson unpacks the logical layers of the dispute, the distinction between implicit and explicit belief, and the key principle that knowledge does not remove possibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari objection
The objector claims: Allah obligated Abu Jahl to believe all that the Prophet brought. The Prophet brought the news that Abu Jahl will not believe. Therefore, Abu Jahl must believe that he will not believe—a contradiction.
This is a standard argument against taklif al-muhal.
2
Examine the Hanafi response: limitation to general rulings
The Hanafī answer: the obligation is only on the general Shari'ah rulings (tawhid, resurrection, reward, punishment, etc.), not on every specific news, such as the report about Abu Jahl's own disbelief. Thus no contradiction arises.
This is the primary defense.
3
Analyse the rebuttal regarding knowledge and possibility
If someone objects that the general rulings themselves are impossible because they contradict the foreknowledge of disbelief, the response is: knowledge (or news) does not change the nature of possibility; it only informs that something will occur, not that it must occur necessarily.
Key principle: al-'ilm yufidu al-wuqu' la al-wujub.
4
Consider the implicit vs. explicit distinction
A further refinement: if the obligation is implicit (ijmālī), does it still entail the contradiction? The text debates whether implicit belief encompasses the specific contradiction. The ultimate Hanafi view: implicit belief also collapses into contradiction because it must correspond to reality, and reality includes non-belief.
This is a secondary, more complex layer.
5
Synthesise the mufta bihi Hanafi position
After analysing all layers, the solid Hanafi position is that the obligation is only on what is possible in itself; the specific news is not part of the obligation. Even if considered implicit, the possibility of faith remains, and obligation is not impossible.
The tarjih supports the rejection of taklif al-muhal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) قالوا :(ثانياً: كلف الله أبا جهل بالإيمان، وهو التصديق بما جاء به النبي ) كله (ومنه) أي بعض ما جاء به أنه لا يصدقه، فقد كلفه بأن يصدقه في أن لا يصدقه) وهو محال، كيف لا (وهو) أي التصدق بعدم التصديق إنما يكون بانتفاء التصديق إذ لو كان التصديق (لعلم) التصديق وصدق به فكيف يصدق بعدمه فإذن التصديق ملزوم لعدم التصديق وملزوم النقيض محال بالذات، فكلف أبو جهل بالمحال بالذات والجواب : أن لا تكليف لأبي جهل (إلا بالتصديق في أحكام الشرع) أنه الله والإخبار بالبعث والنشور والجنة والنار وعذاب القبر من والشفاعة وغير ذلك وعدم التصديق إخبار منه تعالى إليه صلاة الله عليه وآله وأصحابه، وأبو جهل غير مكلف بتصديق إنما يقتضيان أن يكون متعلقهما واقعاً لا كونه واجباً، وبهذا القدر تم الجواب، وزاد بعضهم لو علم أبو جهل بأنه لا يؤمن سقط التكليف، لأنه لا فائدة حينئذ ولم يرتض به المصنف وقال : (وما قيل : لو علم أنه لا يصدقه السقط منه التكليف ممنوع أي باطل فإن الإنسان لم يترك سدى بحال، فلا يسقط عنه التكليف أبداً ، قال في الحاشية وكيف يسقط وإن علمه تعالى إذا لم يكن مانعاً المقدورية فإخباره به وعلم المكلف به أولى أن لا يكون مانعاً فتأمل، وفيه أنه لم يكن القائل بسقوط التكليف قائلاً بانتفاء القدرة بل يقول : إن الفائدة الابتلاء أو الامتثال، ولا يبقى بعد علم المكلف بعدم الوقوع، وسيشير إليه المصنف في مباحث الباب الرابع، لكن الحق ما ذكره ها هنا قيل في الجواب : إنه مكلف بالتصديق بالجميع إجمالاً فهو مكلف أيضاً بتصديق عدم التصديق إجمالاً والتصديق بعدم التصديق إنما يستلزم عدم التصديق إذا كان تفصيلا) لا إذا كان إجمالاً، فالتصديق الإجمالي ليس ملزوماً لعدم التصديق فلا استحالة (أقول : التصديق بالجميع من إجمالاً محال منه فإن هذا الإجمال لا بد أن يكون منطبقاً على هذا التفصيل، وإلا لم يكن إجمالاً له، وإذا كان مطابقاً إلا إذا لم يوجد منه أي من أبي جهل التصديق ولو إجمالاً، وإلا كان كاذباً، فالتصديق الإجمالي أيضاً ملزوم عدم التصديق ولو إجمالاً، وملزوم النقيض محال بالذات فافهم؛ وأيضاً يلزم على الجواب أن الإيمان التفصيلي يكون فرضاً عند الاستفصال، فيلزم الاستحالة قطعاً فتدبر .
And they said: Secondly: Allah obligated Abu Jahl with faith, which is affirming the truth of all that the Prophet brought. And from that which he brought is that he (Abu Jahl) will not affirm him. So He obligated him to affirm him in that he will not affirm him. This is impossible. How not? For affirming the non-affirmation only occurs by the absence of affirmation, since if affirmation existed, affirmation would be known and believed, so how can he affirm its non-existence? Thus affirmation entails non-affirmation, and the entailment of a contradictory is intrinsically impossible. So Abu Jahl was obligated with the intrinsically impossible. The answer: Abu Jahl is only obligated with affirming the rulings of the Sharia — that Allah exists, the news of resurrection, reckoning, paradise, hell, the punishment of the grave, intercession, and other matters. The non-affirmation is a news from Allah to him upon him blessings and peace, and Abu Jahl is not obligated to affirm this news. So he was not obligated to affirm non-affirmation, so there is no impossibility. Thus they said. If you say: The affirmation of the Sharia reports is also impossible from him because it contradicts his news, and contradiction is impossible. He said: Knowledge or news do not remove possibility from the possible, for they only necessitate that their object occurs, not that it is necessary. With this extent the answer is complete. Some added: If Abu Jahl knew that he will not believe, the obligation would fall, because then there is no benefit. The author did not approve and said: What is said — if he knew that he will not affirm, the obligation falls from him — is rejected, i.e., false, for man is not left to no purpose at all, so obligation never falls from him. In the gloss: How can it fall? If Allah's knowledge is not a preventer of capability, then His news and the obligated person's knowledge are even less likely to be preventers. Consider. And therein: The one who said obligation falls did not mean lack of capability, but rather the benefit is trial or compliance, and it does not remain after the obligated person's knowledge of non-occurrence. The author will indicate this in the discussions of the fourth chapter. But the truth is what he mentioned here. It was said in the answer: He is obligated to affirm all of it implicitly, so he is also obligated to affirm non-affirmation implicitly. Affirmation of non-affirmation only entails non-affirmation if it is explicit, not if it is implicit. So implicit affirmation does not entail non-affirmation, so no impossibility. I say: Implicit affirmation of all of it is impossible from him, for this implicit must correspond to this explicit, otherwise it wouldn't be implicit for it. If it corresponds, then affirming all of it is impossible, because then affirmation occurs from him, while it was assumed that there is no affirmation from him, because it was assumed that affirmation is attached to non-affirmation, which entails non-affirmation. So consider. It is not clear with full clarity, for the answerer denied the entailment of attaching affirmation to non-affirmation in implicit attachment, and here he assumes this entailment without explanation. The clearest is to say: Obligation is only with affirmation that corresponds to reality. Implicit affirmation of all that was brought only corresponds if there is no affirmation from him (Abu Jahl), even implicitly. Otherwise, he would be lying. So implicit affirmation also entails non-affirmation, even implicitly, and the entailment of a contradictory is intrinsically impossible. Understand. Also, the answer entails that explicit faith becomes obligatory upon questioning, which inevitably necessitates impossibility. So consider.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute responding to the Ash'ari objection of taklif al-muhal (obligating the impossible). The objection concerns Abu Jahl: Allah obligated him to believe the Prophet's message, yet the Prophet foretold that Abu Jahl would not believe. Thus, believing the Prophet includes believing that he will not believe, which is self-contradictory. The Hanafi author presents a multi-layered response. First, the obligation is limited to the general articles of faith (tawhid, resurrection, etc.) and does not extend to the specific news of his own disbelief. Second, knowledge of future disbelief does not remove possibility; it only informs of what will occur, not that it must occur. Third, the obligation is for the sake of trial, not merely result. The discussion also addresses whether implicit (ijmali) belief avoids the contradiction. The author ultimately concludes that the obligation is to believe in a way that matches reality, and since Abu Jahl's belief would be false, it remains impossible. However, the Hanafi position is that the obligation is not actually impossible because the obligation is only on what is possible in itself, and here the possibility of faith remains despite knowledge. The teacher should note the subtlety: the Hanafis defend divine justice by denying that Allah obligates the impossible, while the Ash'aris argue that Allah may obligate what is impossible as a test of submission.

Key Terms
تكليف بالمحال (taklif bi al-muhal): The proposition that Allah may obligate a person to do something that is intrinsically impossible to fulfill.
تصديق (tasdiq): Affirmation or belief in the truth of something, particularly the message of the Prophet.
إجمال وتفصيل (ijmal wa tafsil): Implicit (general) vs. explicit (detailed) affirmation. Implicit belief does not entail the specific contradictory elements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the text, why was Abu Jahl not obligated with the impossible belief that he will not believe?
A) Because Abu Jahl was not obligated to believe in the Prophet at all.
B) Because God's knowledge of his disbelief removed his capability to believe.
C) Because the obligation was only upon the general articles of faith, not the specific news of his own disbelief.
D) Because Abu Jahl was already a believer in reality.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects obligating the impossible by carefully delimiting the scope of obligation to general, possible matters.

Dispute on Whether Ability Precedes the Act
Inter-madhhab dispute on temporal relation of qudra to the act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for the priority of ability over the act and evaluate the Ash'ari counter-arguments regarding the temporal relation of qudra to taklif.

Core Idea
Ability must precede the act: a condition naturally precedes the conditioned, and obligation of the disbeliever proves it.

This passage delves into a foundational debate in usul al-fiqh between Hanafis and Ash'aris over the temporal relationship between human ability (qudra) and the act. The Hanafi school argues that ability must precede the act for taklif (obligation) to be coherent, while Ash'aris hold that ability is simultaneous. The dispute has practical implications for when a person is considered obligated, especially in cases like the disbeliever's duty to believe. We will unpack the arguments and their logical foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two core Hanafi proofs
First, note the argument that ability is a condition (shart) for a voluntary act, and a condition precedes the conditioned. Second, examine the disbeliever case: if ability were simultaneous, he'd not be obligated to believe before the act, but obligation is real.
The condition precedence is natural, not necessarily temporal—a key nuance.
2
Understand the Ash'ari counter-arguments
The Ash'aris offer three proofs: ability relates like hitting to hit (requiring simultaneity), ability is an accident that doesn't persist, and the act cannot precede itself. Each is refuted by the Hanafi author.
Watch for the rebuttal using Allah's power and the concept of universal nature.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis say a disbeliever is obligated to believe at every moment, even while persisting in disbelief; Ash'aris would say obligation only when ability is present.
This difference affects rulings on the continuous nature of certain obligations.
4
Define istita'a
The author distinguishes istita'a (capability with all conditions) from qudra (generic ability), noting that istita'a is with the act, while qudra precedes it.
This definition reconciles the Ash'ari claim with Hanafi doctrine.
5
Evaluate the dispute's resolution
The Hanafi author claims that al-Ash'ari actually intended the Hanafi position, but his followers misunderstood. The text favors the Hanafi view by refuting each Ash'ari proof.
Note the use of analogy (qiyas) and counterexamples (naqd) in the rebuttals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية في الأحكام الماتريدية (وعند المعتزلة (و) موجودة (معه) لا قبله عند الأشعرية لنا أولاً: أنها شرط الفعل اختياراً، وهو قبل المشروط تدبر فإنه لقائل أن يقول : إن تقدم الشرط على المشروط إنما هو تقدم بالطبع، ولا يجب بحسب الزمان وكان الكلام فيه وفيه غلط باشتراك الاسم، ولعل هذا مشي على ما قاله المتكلمون إن وجود المعلول من الفاعل المختار يكون بعد وجود الاختيار بعدية زمانية، وأن المراد يجب تأخره صريحاً عن إرادة المريد، ولذا امتنعوا من أن يكون معلول المختار قديماً (و) لنا (ثانياً : لو كانت القدرة معه لزم عدم كون الكافر مكلفاً بالإيمان قبله، لأنه غير مقدور له في تلك الحالة ولا تكليف بغير المقدور، ولا تصغ إلى قول من يرى تكليف المحال واقعاً (وأجيب) من قبل الأشعرية (شرط) التكليف عندنا أن يكون هو) أي الفعل نفسه متعلق القدرة (أو يكون (ضده) متعلقاً لها، وها هنا الإيمان، وإن كان غير مقدور للكافر لكن ضده الذي هو الكفر مقدوره البتة، فيصح التكليف (كذا في المواقف) فإن قلت : فعلى هذا يكون تكليف العاجز واقعاً عندهم قاطبة، فلا يصح نسبة الخلاف فيما بينهم قلت : ما سبق هو ما كان المكلف عاجزاً عنه وعن ضده، فلا تنافي، فافهم (أقول :) الإيمان مقدور للكافر البتة، إذ ليس كخلق الجوهر (اتفاقاً فيما بيننا وبينهم، فإنه يستحيل أن يعطي قدرة خلقه بل الكافر عندنا كالساكن القادر على الحركة وعندهم كالمقيد) الغير القادر عليها لا بل عندنا كالمقيد إذ المقيد قادر بالفعل على الحركة، لكن للمانع لا يتحرك، كذلك الكافر قادر على الإيمان، لكن رسوخ العقائد الباطلة منعته عن صرف القدرة إليه وعندهم كالزمن) فإنه غير قادر على الحركة أصلاً (والتفرقة بين إيمان الكافر وحركة الزمن (ضرورية، وإنكارهم مكابرة اعلم أن القدرة المتعلقة بالفعل المستجمعة لجميع الشرائط التي يوجد الفعل بها أو يخلق الله تعالى عندها تسمى استطاعة وهي مع الفعل ،البتة كما روي عن الإمام الهمام في «الوصايا : ولعل مراد الأشعري هذا وأما إنكار القدرة رأساً فالأشعري أجل من أن يتفوه أن يتخذه مذهباً، لكن لما جاء التابعون ولم يتعمقوا في مراده، فهموا أن القدرة لا فيما مر، به فضلاً عن تكون قبل الفعل، ونقلوا هكذا واشتهر فيما بينهم، وقد صرح الإمام فخر الدين الرازي الذي من متبعيه بهذا أيضاً والله أعلم بحال عباده الأشعرية (قالوا : أولاً أنها متعلقة بالمقدور تعلق الضرب بالمضروب، ووجود المتعلق بهذا النحو من التعلق بدون المتعلق محال) وهذا الدليل أيضاً يرشدك إلى أنه أراد بها الاستطاعة المذكورة (قلنا) أولاً (منقوض بقدرة الباري عز وجل، فإن الدليل جار فيها مع أنها ليست مع المقدور وإلا لزم قدم العالم) وثانياً : لا نسلم أنها متعلقة (بل) القدرة (صفة لها صلاحية التعلق فلا تستدعي وجود المقدور (و) قالوا (ثانياً : إنها عرض، وهو لا يبقى زمانين فلو تقدمت على الفعل (لعدمت) عنده (فلم تتعلق بالفعل فانتفت فائدة خلق القدرة (قلنا لا نسلم أن العرض لا يبقى زمانين ولم يقم عليه دليل ولو سلم عدم البقاء فالشرط) في التكليف الطبيعة الكلية لها التي تبقى بتوارد الأمثال) وهي المتقدمة على الفعل لا جزئي معين منها (و) قالوا :(ثالثاً : لا يمكن الفعل قبله) أي قبل نفسه فلا يكون مقدوراً (قبله فإذن ليس القدرة قبل الفعل (وهو) فاسد كما ترى لأنه منقوض بقدرة الباري عز وجل، وأيضاً وصف القبلية على نفسه ممتنعة بالذات، وأما ثبوت إمكان وجودها في زمان قبل زمان وجوده فغیر مستحیل، بل هو ضروري لامتناع الانقلاب فتدبر .
The second article on rulings according to the Maturidis: (And according to the Mu'tazila, ability is) present (with the act), not before it according to the Ash'aris. For us, first: it is a condition for the act performed by choice, and a condition precedes the conditioned. Consider, for one might say that the precedence of a condition over the conditioned is only natural precedence, not necessarily temporal. The discussion here contains an error due to equivocation. Perhaps this follows what the theologians said: the effect of a free agent occurs after the existence of choice in a temporal posteriority, and the intended meaning is that it must be explicitly posterior to the will of the willing agent. Hence they prevented the effect of a free agent from being eternal. (And) for us (secondly): if ability were with the act, it would follow that the disbeliever is not obligated to believe before it, because it is not within his power in that state, and there is no obligation for what is not within one's power. Do not listen to the one who says obligation of the impossible occurs. (And it was answered) by the Ash'aris: The condition of obligation according to us is that (the act itself) is related to ability, or (its opposite) is related to it. Here, faith, though not within the disbeliever's power, its opposite (disbelief) is certainly within his power, so obligation is valid. (Thus in al-Mawaqif). If you say: According to this, obligation of the incapable would be real according to all of them, so disagreement among them cannot be attributed. I say: What preceded is only when the obligated person is incapable of both the act and its opposite, so there is no contradiction. Understand. (I say:) Faith is certainly within the disbeliever's power, for it is not like creating a substance (agreed between us and them; it is impossible for one to be given power to create it). Rather, the disbeliever according to us is like a stationary person able to move, and according to them like one tied (unable to move). No, according to us he is like one tied, for the tied person is actually able to move, but due to an obstacle he does not move. Similarly, the disbeliever is able to believe, but the rootedness of false beliefs prevents him from directing his ability towards it. And according to them he is like a paralyzed person, who is utterly unable to move. (And the distinction between the disbeliever's faith and the paralyzed person's movement is) necessary, and their denial is obstinacy. Know that the ability related to the act, gathering all conditions by which the act exists or Allah creates it, is called 'capability' (istita'a), and it is with the act absolutely, as narrated from the Imam al-Humam in al-Wasaya. Perhaps al-Ash'ari intended this. As for denying ability altogether, al-Ash'ari is too dignified to say that or adopt it as a madhhab. But when the followers came and did not delve into his intention, they understood that ability is not before the act, and they transmitted it thus, and it became famous among them. Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, one of his followers, also stated this. Allah knows best about the state of His servants the Ash'aris. (They said:) First, it (ability) is related to the possible in the manner of hitting to the hit, and the existence of the related in this manner without the object of relation is impossible. This proof also guides you that he intended by it the mentioned capability. (We say) first: (it is rebutted by the ability of Allah Almighty, for the proof applies to it while it is not with the possible, otherwise the world would be eternal). Second: We do not accept that it is related; rather, ability is a quality having the potential for relation, so it does not necessitate the existence of the possible. (And they said) second: It (ability) is an accident, and it does not remain for two moments. So if it precedes the act, it would perish at the time of the act, and thus would not relate to the act, and the benefit of creating ability would be nullified. (We say) we do not accept that an accident does not remain for two moments, and no proof has been established for it. Even if non-remaining is conceded, the condition in obligation is its universal nature, which persists through the succession of similars, and it is prior to the act, not a particular instance of it. (And they said) third: The act cannot exist before it (the act itself), so it cannot be possible before it. Therefore ability is not before the act. (This is) corrupt as you see, because it is rebutted by the ability of Allah Almighty. Also, description of priority concerning itself is intrinsically impossible. As for establishing the possibility of its existence in a time before the time of its existence, it is not impossible; rather it is necessary to prevent conversion. So reflect.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute about the temporal relationship of ability (qudra) to the act in the context of taklif (legal obligation). The author opens by stating that according to the Maturidis (and Mu'tazila, as per the matn), ability exists with the act, while the Ash'aris hold it is before the act. The Hanafi position, as defended here, is that ability must precede the act. The first argument is that ability is a condition for the voluntary act, and a condition naturally precedes the conditioned; however, this precedence is not necessarily temporal but can be natural. The text warns against equivocation. The second argument addresses the case of the disbeliever: if ability were only with the act, the disbeliever would not be obligated to believe before the act, but that is false because he is commanded to believe now. The Ash'ari response is that the condition for obligation is that either the act or its opposite be within one's power; here, disbelief (the opposite) is within the disbeliever's power, so obligation is valid. The Hanafi author counters by explaining that the disbeliever is actually like a tied person who has the ability but is prevented by an obstacle, unlike a paralyzed person who has no ability. The text then defines 'istita'a' (capability) as the ability that gathers all conditions and is simultaneous with the act, attributing this view to al-Ash'ari himself, suggesting a misunderstanding by his followers. The passage then examines three Ash'ari proofs: (1) ability relates to the possible like hitting to the hit, so they must coexist; (2) ability is an accident that does not persist, so if prior it would perish; (3) the act cannot be before itself, so ability cannot be prior. The Hanafi rebuttal uses the analogy of Allah's ability (which is not with the possible), rejects the premise that accidents do not persist, and points out that priority is predicated on time, not essence. The lesson underscores the Hanafi commitment to a logically coherent account of human agency and divine command.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Ability or power to perform an act; a quality by which one can act or refrain.
الاستطاعة (al-istita'a): The ability that gathers all conditions, which is simultaneous with the act according to the author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is the disbeliever obligated to believe before actually believing?
A) Because belief and disbelief are both within his power simultaneously.
B) Because disbelief (the opposite) is within his power, fulfilling the condition for obligation.
C) Because ability exists with the act, so obligation is valid only at the moment of belief.
D) Because the disbeliever is like a paralyzed person who has no ability at all.

Key Takeaway
Ability must logically precede the act for obligation to be meaningful; the Hanafi argument employs natural priority and the case of the disbeliever to defend this.

Renewed Capability: Condition for Qada or Not?
Expanding on whether renewed capability is a condition for qada obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether renewed capability is required for the obligation of qada, identify the key dalil and counter-arguments, and apply the usul principle of continuity of obligation.

Core Idea
The obligation of qada persists in the liability even without capability; only performance requires capability.

In this passage, the author delves into a subtle usul question: does a person need to have capability (qudra) at the moment of performing qada for the obligation to be valid? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the persistence of the obligation in the liability (dhimma) and the actual demand to perform. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how obligations survive even when immediate performance is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
What is the core question about renewed capability and the obligation of qada? The passage explores whether capability at the time of qada is a condition for the obligation itself.
2
Trace the opposing arguments
List the four arguments (wujuh) presented against the Hanafi view. They include: (1) qada is a new taklif, (2) continuity of capability may be required, (3) taklif with the impossible is invalid, (4) the sleeper is exempt from taklif yet must perform qada.
These are the 'aspects' (wujuh) mentioned in the text.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the author rebut each of the four arguments? For instance, he argues that the liability remains from the original obligation, and qada is a continuation, not a new taklif.
Focus on the distinction between the persistence of the obligation and the performance demand.
4
Examine the key dalil
The verse 'لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها' is cited by opponents. How does the Hanafi scholar specify this verse to apply only to initial obligations (ada), not to the persistent liability for qada?
The specification is based on texts on qada and ijma on sin for delay.
5
Synthesize the final Hanafi position
State the clear Hanafi view: the obligation of qada remains in the liability without requiring capability; capability is only required for actual performance. If lost, the person must make a will or faces sin.
This is the muftā bihī position.

Source Text

القدرة المتجددة شرطاً لوجوب القضاء، ففي النفس الأخير يجب قضاء الواجبات التي في الذمة، وفيه نظر من وجوه :
الأول : أنا قد بينا أن مقتضى اتحاد السبب ليس إلا أن وجوب القضاء، لتفريغ ذمة اشتغلت بالواجب، كما أن وجوب الأداء كان لتفريغها والتكليف الذي هو طلب القضاء غير تكليف الأداء، فإنه طلب مثله، وإن كان السبب فيهما واحداً وكان التكليف بالأداء متضمناً إياه عند فواته ونص القضاء كاشفاً عنه، وكذا نفس الوجوب واحد، فهذا ليس من باب التكليف، وإذا كان التكليف متجدداً فلا بد من قدرة متجددة .
الثاني : سلمنا أن تكليف القضاء بقاء تكليف الأداء، لكن لا يلزم منه عدم اشتراط القدرة للقضاء لجواز أن يكون بقاء القدرة شرطاً لبقاء الواجب، كما أنها شرط لابتداء الواجب
الثالث : أن الدليل الدال على امتناع التكليف بالمحال ناهضها هنا، فإن التكليف به يتوقف على تصورها إيقاعاً، وذلك مستحيل في النفس الأخير، وأيضاً أنه سفه وعبث، فيستحيل عليه تعالى .

قال بعض المشايخ: إن الأداء والقضاء سيان في اشتراط القدرة (٢) والأداء كما يشترط لوجوبها أداء عيناً القدرة الحقيقية، ويكتفي بالمتوهمة فيما يجب الأداء لترتب القضاء، كذلك القضاء يشترط القدرة الحقيقية للإتيان بها عيناً، وإذا أخر إلى النفس الأخير يكتفي بالقدرة المتوهمة لاحتمال امتداد هذا النفس، لكن لا ، لأن يجب عليه القضاء عيناً بل ليترتب عليه الخلف وهو الإيصاء أو الإثم بعد الموت وهذا أيضاً قريب مما ذكر، والحاصل أن نفس اشتغال الذمة بالقضاء لا يشترط له القدرة لبقاء الاشتغال بكل الواجبات، وأما طلب إيقاعها تفريغاً للذمة فيشترط القدرة له أداء كان أو قضاء ابتداء، وبقاء هذا هو الذي يقتضيه الفحص ؛ فإن أرادوا بحقيقة الحال هذا القدر فكلامهم تام وإلا فمشكل، والله أعلم .

فهم المكلف الخطاب شرط التكليف عندنا المراد بالفهم نفس التصور لا التصديق، وإلا لم يكن الكافر مكلفاً لعدم التصديق، ويلزم الدور، كذا في الحاشية»، ولزوم الدور لأجل

(۲) قوله: (والأداء كما يشترط) الخ كذا في الأصل وانظر .
Second article on rulings. 113. Renewed capability is a condition for the obligation of qada. So in the last moment, the qada of obligations that are in the liability is obligatory. And there is consideration from several aspects: First: We have explained that the implication of the unity of cause is only that the obligation of qada is to discharge a liability occupied with the obligation, just as the obligation of ada was to discharge it. And the taklif which is the demand of qada is different from the taklif of ada, for it is a demand of its like, even if the cause for both is one, and the taklif of ada implicitly contained it upon its loss, and the text of qada is a revealer of it. Similarly, the obligation itself is one, so this is not from the category of taklif. And if taklif is renewed, then renewed capability is necessary. Second: We concede that the taklif of qada is a continuation of the taklif of ada, but it does not follow from that the non-requirement of capability for qada, because it is possible that the continuation of capability is a condition for the continuation of the obligation, just as it is a condition for the beginning of the obligation. Third: The evidence indicating the impossibility of taklif with the impossible is operative here, for taklif with it depends on its conception as an occurrence, and that is impossible in the last moment. Also, it is foolish and vain, so it is impossible for Him, exalted. Fourth: The sleeper is not subject to taklif, yet qada is obligatory upon him, so in qada there is a new taklif, so capability is necessary. Similarly for the traveler regarding fasting. (Also, if qada were not obligatory except with renewed capability, he would not be sinful for abandoning it without excuse, and they have consensus on making sinful. The demonstration of the correlation: the one obligated may delay the qada prayer and fasting to the last moment, and there capability is lost. So if the obligation fell, he would not be sinful, since the delay was permissible, and there is no sin in the permissible. And in the last moment, the obligation has been removed, so no sin either. And there is consideration. First: because it would necessitate that capability is not a condition for Hajj and all lifelong obligations other than qada, for he may delay to the end of life, and capability is negated, so he would not be sinful. Unless they commit to not requiring continuation of capability for continuation of the obligation, even if there were no qada, as indicated by the first evidence. Second: because the permissible delay is delay to the last times of life that accommodate performing qada. If he delays beyond that time to the last moment, he is sinful for his act of non-legitimate delay. So then it is possible that capability is required for qada, and he may delay to the last times of capability, not to the time when capability is lost. Then when the text 'Allah does not charge a soul except [within] its capacity' [2:286] was brought against him, he answered by saying: So it specifies the verse 'Allah does not charge a soul except its capacity' to ada. If you say: Where is the specifying factor? He answered: The texts on qada of fasting and prayer have specified it, for they encompass the capable and others. Thus they said. And there is consideration in it, for why would these texts not be specified by this verse? Rather, reason also indicates the specification of those texts, for seeking compliance from the incapable is among intellectual impossibilities, so it is not permissible for Him, exalted. (I say: If the obligation is established in the last part) like one who becomes eligible therein (and capability is absent in qada, then making sinful is problematic) due to lack of negligence from him in abandoning ada nor in abandoning qada. And Allah knows best what is correct. And this is not sound because they do not make sinful in this case (1). Then know: The liability has become occupied with ada and remained after the time elapsed, so he was commanded to discharge it by performing its like. So the obligation that was established in the liability is definitely one. So we say: Capability is not required for the continuation of this occupation, because it is a continuation of a prior obligation that he was capable of discharging but did not, so it remained occupied in the last moment, so he is demanded to will for its discharge, and capability for that is present. And if this capability also does not remain, then in exchange for this occupation and obligation, there remains forgiveness or sin. This is a reasonable matter and nothing refutes it, and both evidences are complete. The formulation of the first: the occupation of the liability with ada remains at the time of qada, and the command for it is a command to discharge that liability, and capability is not required for this occupation, and this occupation is not from the category of taklif. Similarly, the sleeping person's liability was occupied during sleep. The formulation of the second: if there were nothing in the liability, there would be no basis for making sinful, and that is clear. And there is no need to specify the noble verse 'Allah does not charge...' etc., because this occupation is not a taklif. It would only be if he were demanded to discharge it without capability. Some mashayikh said: Ada and qada are equal in requiring capability (2). And just as for the obligation of ada in kind, real capability is required, and imagined capability suffices for what is obligatory of ada due to the consequence of qada, similarly for qada, real capability is required for performing it in kind, and if he delays to the last moment, imagined capability suffices due to the possibility of that moment extending. But no, because he is not obliged to do qada in kind but rather the alternative upon it, which is will or sin after death. And this is also close to what was mentioned. The summary: The occupation of the liability with qada itself does not require capability due to the continuation of occupation with all obligations. As for demanding its occurrence to discharge the liability, capability is required for it, whether ada or qada initially. And the continuation of this is what investigation necessitates. So if they intend by the reality of the matter this extent, then their speech is complete, otherwise it is problematic. And Allah knows best. Chapter Four: On the One Ruled Upon, Who Is the Mukallaf. Issue: The mukallaf's understanding of the address is a condition for taklif according to us. By understanding is meant the mere conception, not affirmation, otherwise the disbeliever would not be mukallaf due to lack of affirmation, and circularity would follow. Thus in the hashya. And circularity because of (1) ... (2) ...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses a central usul al-fiqh issue: whether renewed capability (qudra mutajaddida) is a condition for the obligation of make-up (qada) when one has missed an obligatory act like prayer or fasting. The author presents multiple arguments and counterarguments. The first four aspects (wujuh) argue that qada is a new taklif distinct from the original obligation (ada), therefore requiring capability at the time of performance. But the text then refines: the liability (dhimma) remains occupied by the missed obligation, and the demand to discharge it is not a new taklif but a continuation of the previous duty. Hence, capability is not required for the persistence of the obligation in the liability, but it is required for the actual performance. A key proof is the consensus (ijma) that one who delays qada to the last moment of life is sinful, which would be impossible if lack of capability removed the obligation entirely. The author also discusses the Quranic verse 'لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها' and how it applies to ada, not to the persistent liability. The passage concludes with the view of some mashayikh that ada and qada are symmetrical in requiring capability for performance but not for the underlying obligation. The overall ruling is that the obligation of qada remains in the liability without need for capability, but the duty to perform it actively (or to make a will if unable) requires capability. This is a classic Hanafi position emphasizing the moral responsibility of the mukallaf and the continuity of obligation.

Key Terms
القدرة المتجددة (al-qudra al-mutajaddida): Renewed capability that arises at the time of performing qada, distinct from the capability at the time of the original obligation.
القضاء (al-qada): The make-up act performed to discharge a missed obligatory act (ada).
التكليف (al-taklif): The divine address that imposes an obligation; requires understanding (fahm) of the address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position discussed, what is the effect of losing capability (qudra) in the last moment of life on the obligation of qada?
A) The obligation of qada drops completely.
B) The obligation of qada remains in the liability, but actual performance is not required; instead, a will or sin follows.
C) The obligation is transferred to a fine (kaffara).
D) The obligation is postponed until after death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the obligation of qada persists in the liability without requiring renewed capability; only its performance requires capability.

Interpreting the Quranic Prohibition of Prayer During Intoxication
Textual analysis of Quran 4:43 using Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of literal meaning (haqiqah) to derive the ruling from Quran 4:43 and evaluate the opposing interpretation.

Core Idea
The verse prohibits prayer while intoxicated, not drinking; al-ilm means certainty, not mere knowledge.

This passage examines the Hanafi interpretation of the Quranic verse that seems to forbid approaching prayer while intoxicated. The author clarifies that the key term 'ilm' denotes certainty, and the verse only prohibits performing prayer in a state of drunkenness, not the act of drinking itself. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper usul al-fiqh analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and key phrase
Locate the Quranic verse (4:43) and the operative phrase 'حَتَّى تَعْلَمُوا مَا تَقُولُونَ'. This phrase is the focus of the usul analysis.
The full verse is: 'يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَىٰ حَتَّىٰ تَعْلَمُوا مَا تَقُولُونَ'.
2
Classify the term 'العلم'
Determine whether 'العلم' is used in its literal sense (haqiqah) or metaphorically (majaz). According to Hanafi usul, the literal meaning takes precedence unless impossible.
The author argues that 'العلم' means certainty (اليقين الواقعي) in the literal sense.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The principle 'الحقيقة مقدمة على المجاز' (literal meaning is given precedence over metaphorical) is applied. Also, the imperative 'لا تقربوا' indicates a prohibition (nahy) which implies tahrim (prohibition) in Hanafi usul.
The prohibition is conditional: 'حَتَّى تَعْلَمُوا' means 'until you know (with certainty)'.
4
Derive the ruling
The ruling is that performing prayer in a state of intoxication (where one does not have certainty of speech) is prohibited (haram). The verse does not prohibit drinking alcohol itself, as the condition is about prayer time.
This is supported by the historical context (asbab al-nuzul) where companions continued to drink but avoided prayer times.
5
Evaluate the opposing interpretation
Some interpreters claim the verse prohibits intoxication entirely. The Hanafi response is that the literal and contextual reading does not support that; the verse only addresses the prayer condition.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether drinking was still permissible after this verse.

The second article on rulings. The meaning of his saying: So consider its severe degree, for the weak is deficient in one aspect. For if you say: When the intoxicated person is understanding, what about His saying: 'until you know what you are saying'? He said: And the meaning of 'until you know what you are saying' is 'until you are certain of what you are saying'. And this that we mentioned has no interpretation (ta'wil) in it, for 'knowledge' in language is actual certainty, nothing else except metaphorically. And in some copies: 'And this is an interpretation,' and no justification appears for it, perhaps it is from the scribe's oversight, unless he means that this is an interpretation (ta'wil) not an explanation (tafsir), for explaining by opinion is forbidden, and the people adhered to the interpretation that it is a prohibition of intoxication during prayer, so the meaning is: Do not become intoxicated so that you pray while intoxicated, like their saying: 'Do not die while you are unjust,' i.e., do not be unjust so that you die unjustly. If you say: The context of revelation does not support this, for wine remained permissible after the revelation of this verse as detailed in the commentaries, I say: The meaning is a prohibition of intoxication at the time of prayer, i.e., do not become intoxicated at the time of prayer so that you pray while intoxicated. And in that incident, they left the time of prayer, and it (wine) did not remain permissible after the revelation of this verse except at times other than prayer times. So reflect.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Quranic verse (4:43) regarding prayer and intoxication. The author explains that the verse does not prohibit drinking alcohol but rather prohibits performing prayer while in a state of drunkenness. He emphasizes that the word 'علم' (knowledge) in this context means certainty (اليقين), not mere awareness. The author refutes an alternative interpretation that would prohibit drinking altogether, arguing from the historical context (شأن النزول) that wine remained permissible after this verse except at prayer times. The Hanafi position is that drinking alcohol is prohibited by other proofs, but this particular verse only addresses the prohibition of prayer while intoxicated. The commentary also addresses the difference between interpretation (ta'wil) and explanation (tafsir), cautioning against interpreting based on personal opinion.

Key Terms
العلم (al-ilm): In this context, certainty (اليقين الواقعي), not mere knowledge.
السكر (al-sukr): Intoxication that prevents understanding of one's speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Do not drink alcohol at all.
B) Do not pray until you are certain of what you are saying.
C) Do not become intoxicated so that you can pray.
D) Do not say anything until you know it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul analysis of Quran 4:43 shows that the verse only prohibits prayer while intoxicated, not the act of drinking; the word 'ilm' must be taken in its literal sense of certainty.

Hanafi Response to Mu'tazila: One Speech, Finite Relations
Refuting Mu‘tazila arguments against pre-eternity of speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi concept of al-ta’alluq al-i‘tibārī to refute the Mu‘tazila argument of infinite regress in divine speech.

Core Idea
Divine speech is one attribute; multiplicity is mental, and objects are finite — no infinite regress.

This passage tackles one of the most potent Mu‘tazila objections against the pre-eternity of the Qur’an: if Allah’s speech is eternal, then there would be infinite commands for infinite non-existent individuals, leading to impossible infinite regress (tasalsul). The Hanafi response defends the unity of the divine attribute of speech by distinguishing between the attribute itself and its relations (ta‘alluqāt), which are mental (i‘tibārī) and limited to finite obligated beings. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications for uṣūl al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Extract the two Mu‘tazila arguments: (1) infinite regress from infinite non-existent individuals, (2) equal relation to all acts leading to contradictory commands.
The first objection is about multiplicity, the second about indiscriminateness.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to the first objection
Study the Hanafi counter: speech is one pre-eternal attribute like knowledge; multiplicity is only in mental relations (i‘tibārī); the non-existent are finite (Adam to Resurrection), so no infinite regress.
Key concept: al-ta‘alluq al-i‘tibārī.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the second objection
The Mu‘tazila argued that if speech is eternal, it would relate equally to all acts, requiring a cause to differentiate command from prohibition. Hanafis reply that good and evil are intrinsic in some acts, so command/prohibition attach based on the act’s nature.
This rejects the premise that ḥusn and qubḥ are purely shar‘ī.
4
Critique the Ash‘arite alternative
The text mentions that Ash‘arites answer by saying an attribute may selectively relate (like power). The Hanafi critique: this is arbitrary preference without a preferrer (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ), which is unsound.
This highlights a methodological flaw in the Ash‘arite response.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilāf
The practical consequence: Hanafis affirm the pre-eternity of speech as a single attribute of Allāh; Mu‘tazila deny it, considering the Qur’ān created.
This has implications for the status of the Qur’ān in fiqh.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الخطاب فإن المتعلق بزيد غير المتعلق بعمرو والجواب) أن لا تعدد في الخطاب المتعلق بالذات (وإن التعدد العارض له بحسب تعدد التعلقات تعدد اعتباري فإنه أي الخطاب (صفة واحدة أزلية لا تعدد فيه كالعلم والقدرة، وانقسامه إلى الأنواع والأفراد بحسب التعلقات لا باختلاف الذاتيات كانقسامها (هذا) فإن قلت هب أن التعدد فيه بحسب اعتباري، لكن التعلقات ليست اختراعية محضة بل لها حظ من الثبوت الواقعي والإلزام كون الأوامر It necessarily requires the actual existence of the divisions. As for the intention of addressing what will be, it only requires the realization of the divisions in it, and the secret is that addressing is only in actualized relation, so there is no relation in pre-eternity except in the sense of the validity of communication, nothing else, and it does not require the divisions actually. You may say that He, glorified and exalted, knows in pre-eternity the responsible individuals themselves, and that at the time of their existence with the conditions of obligation they are commanded such and such and prohibited from such and such, or He does not know. On the second possibility, it follows that obligation would not be realized in the future either, because God did not know that, which is false. So the first is determined, thus rational command and prohibition are established, so some division must exist. Also, the non-existent is not obligated at that time, i.e., when speech existed and did not become command or prohibition or any of the divisions, since there is no relation of speech to the action of the obligated at that time. It may be answered by accepting that the non-existent is not obligated according to him, but this is corrupt because the objection of foolishness and frivolity was only about deeming the obligation of the non-existent permissible; when that is denied, the objection has no direction, so the escape is not valid in this way. Al-Qattan said this speech as an escape from the mentioned objection, unless it is said that the Mu'tazila used to raise the objection of foolishness and frivolity against the pre-eternity of speech, so he escaped with this. The truth is that there is no disagreement between him and the majority regarding the pre-eternity of suspended obligation, as the author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya said. Perhaps he meant by the negated command and prohibition the actualized command and prohibition. Then it reverts to what the majority held, and then there is no doubt that the occurrence of these accidents in the future is certain, and on this, nothing from the mentioned objections applies to him. And the Mu'tazila said: if speech is pre-eternal, then the pre-eternality of non-finiteness follows, for the non-existent are infinite, and so is what relates to them of speech, for that which relates to Zayd is different from that which relates to 'Amr. The answer: there is no multiplicity in speech related to the essence, and the multiplicity that accrues to it according to the multiplicity of relations is a mental multiplicity. For it, i.e., speech, is one pre-eternal attribute, no multiplicity in it, like knowledge and power. Its division into types and individuals is according to relations, not by difference of essences, like their division. This: if you say: even if multiplicity in it is mental, but the relations are not purely invented; rather they have a share of actual existence, and the implication is that the commands and prohibitions are invented, so infinite regress follows. I say: the meaning of their being actual is that when speech is compared to its object, it is valid that the relation be abstracted from it, not that the relation is an existing entity in reality. Reflect. Then the problem from the beginning is that the obligated individuals are limited between the existence of Adam (peace be upon him) and the Resurrection, so they are finite, and so are the relations. Reflect on this. And they said secondly: if speech were pre-eternal, its relation to everything would be equal, and according to you, good and evil are positive [by revelation], so it is valid to relate to everything; thus it would follow that command and prohibition relate to a single action. We say: we do not accept that good and evil are positive; rather some things are good and some are evil, so command relates to that part and prohibition to this part. This objection only applies to the Ash'arites, and they answered that a thing valid for relation to multiple things may relate to some and not to others like power. But there is in this that the relation of an attribute to some when it is valid to relate to all is a preference without a preferrer, and this is contrary to wisdom. Dropped relations. Reflect.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to Mu'tazila objections against the pre-eternity of divine speech (kalam). The author first explains that pre-eternal speech does not require actual division of commands and prohibitions because it is a single attribute; multiplicity is only in relations (ta'alluqat), which are mental (i'tibari). The Mu'tazila argue that if speech is eternal, there would be infinite commands for infinite non-existent individuals, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul). The Hanafi response: (1) The speech itself is one, like knowledge; multiplicity is in relations, not in the essence. (2) Even if relations have some reality, the non-existent individuals are finite (from Adam to Resurrection), so no infinite regress. The second objection is that pre-eternal speech would relate equally to all acts, so both command and prohibition could attach to the same act. The Hanafis reject the premise that good and evil are purely positive (shar'i); some acts are intrinsically good or evil, so command/prohibition attach accordingly. The Ash'arite answer (that capability may selectively apply) is criticized as arbitrary preference without a preferrer. The passage concludes by noting that the true position aligns with the majority (jamhur) that obligation is pre-eternal in a suspended (ta'liqi) sense.

Key Terms
التعلق (al-ta‘alluq): The relation between a divine attribute (e.g., speech) and its object (e.g., a commanded act); this relation is mental (i‘tibārī), not real multiplication of the attribute.
المعدوم (al-ma‘dūm): A non-existent entity; the text argues that non-existent individuals are finite (between Adam and Resurrection), so commands relating to them are finite.
التسلسل (al-tasalsul): Infinite regress; an objection raised by the Mu‘tazila if commands multiply infinitely for infinite non-existent individuals. The Hanafi response denies the infinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why does the pre-eternity of speech not lead to infinite commands?
A) Because the non-existent individuals are infinite, but commands are only for existents.
B) Because speech is one attribute; multiplicity is only mental, and the non-existent are finite.
C) Because commands and prohibitions are not created until the moment of obligation.
D) Because the Mu‘tazila do not accept pre-eternity of speech.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the unity of divine speech by treating multiplicity of commands as mental relations (i‘tibārī) and affirming the finitude of obligated beings.

Hanafi Accountability for Error: Crime, Shubha, and Consequences
Dispute on whether errors are punishable and their civil/criminal effects in Hanafi law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accountability for error, identify the Quranic dalil, and explain how shubha waives criminal punishment while preserving financial liability.

Core Idea
Error is a crime due to underlying negligence, but shubha removes hadd and qisas while leaving financial liability and divorce valid.

Can a person be held accountable for actions done by mistake? The Mu'tazila argue that only intentional acts are crimes, but the Hanafis hold that error involves a prior failure of caution, making it a form of crime. This lesson explores the rational and revealed basis for Hanafi accountability, its limits, and how it applies to property damage, manslaughter, and divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and parties
State the central issue: whether error (khata) can be a basis for legal accountability. The Hanafis say yes (rationally), the Mu'tazila say no. Note that this is a usul dispute about the nature of crime.
The Hanafi position is that error is a crime because it arises from negligence (adam al-tathabbut).
2
Analyse the Hanafi Quranic proof
Examine verse 2:285-286 where believers ask not to be held accountable for error. The Hanafis argue that if error were not punishable, this request would be for something impossible, which would not be praised. Therefore, accountability is possible.
The verse uses the imperative 'la tu'akhidhna' (do not hold us accountable), implying accountability is a real possibility.
3
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal of the Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila claim crime requires intent (qasd). The Hanafis respond: error is not simply an act without intent; it is caused by a failure to be cautious (adam al-tathabbut), which is a volitional act. Hence error itself is a crime, though the element of doubt (shubha) mitigates revealed punishments.
The Hanafis distinguish between rational accountability (possible) and revealed punishment (waived due to shubha).
4
Apply the principles to practical effects
Work through the specific rulings: (1) hadd and qisas are dropped because of shubha; (2) financial liability for property damage remains; (3) expiation and diya are due for accidental killing; (4) a mistaken person's divorce is valid (unlike the Shafi'i view) because the utterance is taken as a sign (mazanna) of intent.
The divorce ruling illustrates how the law uses apparent signs when direct intent is hard to verify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة المؤاخذة بالخطأ جائزة عقلاً) أي العقل لا يأبى عن تجويز المؤاخذة على ارتكاب السيئة خطأ (خلافاً للمعتزلة لنا أنه تعالى مدح السائلين عدم المؤاخذة بالخطأ قال الله تعالى : وَقَالُوا سَمِعْنَا وَأَطَعْنَا غُفرانك ربنا وإليك المصير لا يكلف اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ رَبَّنَا لَا تُؤَاخِذْنَا إِن نَّسِينَا أَوْ أَخْطَأْنَا ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٥ - ٢٨٦] ولو لم تصح المؤاخذة عقلاً لما مدحوا بهذا السؤال لأنه حينئذ سؤال بما يستحيل (والسؤال بما يستحيل باطل) المعتزلة (قالوا : (المؤاخذة إنما تكون بالجناية) وهي (بالقصد) ولا قصد في الخطأ فلا جناية، فلا مؤاخذة فيه (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه لا جناية فيه بل فيه جناية (بعدم التثبت والاحتياط الواجبين والخطأ لما كان مسبباً عن عدم التثبت الذي هو الجناية صار هو أيضاً جناية، فتجوز المؤاخذة به أيضاً، ولسنا نقول : إن المؤاخذة بعدم التثبت فقط، بل بفعل الخطأ، حتى يرد أن النزاع حينئذ لفظي، بل المؤاخذة به لكن لكونه مسبباً عن فعل اختياري فتدبر، ثم الخطأ وإن كان جناية كما بينا إلا أن فيه شبهة العدم أي شبهة عدم الجناية، ولذا لا يؤاخذ به في الإثم سمعاً، كما قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (إن الله تجاوز عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما أكرهوا عليه» (فلا يؤاخذ بحد ولا قصاص لأنهما يسقطان بالشبهات دون ضمان (المتلفات) خطأ من الأموال فإنه يؤاخذ به جبراً للمتلف لا لكونه جناية، ألا ترى أنه يجب على الصغير، ولما كان نوع جناية والقتل من أعظم الكبائر لم يهدر الخطأ فيه بل وجبت الكفارة وأما الدية فجزاء المحل (ويقع طلاقه عندنا وكل إنشاء لا يحتمل الفسخ (خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله (لأن اعتبار الكلام) إنما يكون بالقصد ولم يوجد في الخاطىء فلا اعتبار لكلامه (كما في النائم فلا يقع نعم اعتبار الكلام بالقصد، لكن الغفلة عن معنى اللفظ أمر خفي فلا تناط الأحكام على قصد المعنى (فأقيم تمييزاً لبلوغ مقامه أي القصد لأنه مظنة القصد، وإذا كانت المظنة موجودة لا
Issue: Holding (someone) accountable for error is rationally permissible – i.e., reason does not forbid allowing accountability for committing a bad act by mistake – contrary to the Mu'tazila. Our proof: Allah praised those who ask for not being held accountable for error. Allah said: 'They say: We hear and obey, (grant us) Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return. Allah does not burden a soul more than it can bear. It has what it earns and it is responsible for what it acquires. Our Lord, do not hold us accountable if we forget or err' (2:285-286). If accountability for error were not rationally valid, they would not have been praised for this question, because then they would be asking for something impossible, and asking for the impossible is false. The Mu'tazila said: Accountability is only for a crime, and crime is by intention; there is no intention in error, so no crime, so no accountability. We reply: We do not grant that there is no crime in it; rather there is a crime in it – due to failing to be firm and to take the necessary precautions. Since error is caused by lack of firmness, which is the crime, it also becomes a crime, so accountability for it is permissible. We do not say that accountability is only for the lack of firmness; rather it is for the act of error, so that the dispute would be a verbal one. Rather, accountability is for it, but because it is caused by a volitional act – so reflect. Then error, although it is a crime as we explained, has the doubt (shubha) of absence – i.e., the doubt that it is not a crime. Therefore, one is not held accountable for sin according to revelation, as the Messenger of Allah said: 'Allah has pardoned my nation for error, forgetfulness, and what they are forced to do.' So one is not held accountable for hadd or qisas, because they are dropped due to doubts, except for liability for (damage to) property by mistake – for that one is held accountable to compensate for the damage, not because it is a crime. Do you not see that it is obligatory even from a minor? And since it is a type of crime and killing is one of the greatest enormities, error in it is not neglected; rather expiation becomes obligatory, and the blood money is compensation for the place. And divorce by a mistaken person occurs according to us, and every constructive (insha'i) statement that does not admit of revocation – contrary to al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him – because consideration of speech is only by intention, and intention is not present in the mistaken person, so his speech has no consideration, as with a sleeping person – it does not occur. Yes, consideration of speech is by intention, but heedlessness of the meaning of the word is a subtle matter, so rulings are not attached to the intention of the meaning. So a distinction is established to reach its position – i.e., intention – because it is the apparent sign of intention. And when the apparent sign exists, it is not ...
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage tackles the rational and revealed ruling on accountability for actions done by mistake (khata). The Hanafi position is that such accountability is rationally possible, contrary to the Mu'tazila who argue that punishment requires intentional crime. The Hanafi proof is from the Quran where believers ask for forgiveness for error, implying it is possible to be held accountable (otherwise the request would be impossible). The text argues that error involves a prior failure (adam al-tathabbut) which is a form of negligence, hence a crime. However, due to the doubt (shubha) about intent, revealed punishments like hadd and qisas are waived, but financial liability remains because it compensates loss, not punishes the crime. For killing by mistake, expiation (kaffara) and blood money (diya) are due. Then the passage discusses the Hanafi rule that a mistaken person’s divorce is valid, unlike the Shafi'i view. The Hanafi justification is that while intention (qasd) is generally required, heedlessness of the specific meaning is subtle and not easily verifiable; therefore, the law considers the apparent sign (the utterance itself) as a proof of intent for such irrevocable statements. The passage ends mid-sentence on this point.

Key Terms
الخطأ (al-khata): An act done mistakenly without intent, but arising from a failure to be cautious.
الشبهة (al-shubha): A doubt that prevents the application of hadd or qisas.
المظنة (al-mazanna): An apparent sign that stands in for an actual condition; here, the utterance of divorce is taken as proof of intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, why is divorce by a mistaken person considered valid despite the lack of intent?
A) Because the intention of divorce is present in every utterance.
B) Because the utterance itself is taken as an apparent sign (mazanna) of intent.
C) Because the Shafi'i view is rejected entirely.
D) Because error has no effect on divorce.

Key Takeaway
Error (khata) is legally significant: it is a crime due to prior negligence, but shubha (doubt) removes criminal punishments while preserving financial liability, expiation for killing, and validity of divorce.

The Positor of Language: Divine Tawqif vs. Human Convention
Defending the Ash'ari view of divine tawqif through Quranic evidence and interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ash'ari position on the wadi' of language, identify the Quranic proof they cite, and explain the Hanafi response to the objection that 'names' refers to realities.

Core Idea
The Teaching of Names does not automatically prove Divine Tawqif; the meaning of 'names' is contested.

In Hanafi usul, one of the foundational questions is how language came to be: was it divinely taught (tawqif) or human convention (istilah)? This passage presents the Ash'ari argument that language is divinely placed, using the Quranic verse about Adam. But the verse is not straightforward; it requires careful interpretation to support the claim. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the counter-argument, sharpening your skills in analyzing scriptural proofs for usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue: Who is the wadi'?
The passage states there is disagreement over the identity of the positor of language. The Ash'ari school holds that Allah is the wadi' via divine tawqif. Understand that this is an usul dispute with implications for the authority of linguistic conventions.
The Hanafi school generally accepts tawqif but does not entirely reject human convention.
2
State the Ash'ari dalil from the Qur'an
The Ash'ari proof is the verse 'And He taught Adam all the names' (al-Baqara 31). They interpret 'names' as the words themselves, and the teaching as the act of placing these words. Therefore, Allah is the positor.
The dalil is a direct Quranic text with qat'i thubut but zanni dalala regarding the meaning of 'names'.
3
Examine the objection: 'names' might mean realities
An objection is raised: perhaps 'names' refers to the named entities (realities), not the words. Knowing realities is true perfection, and that is what Allah taught Adam. This would undermine the Ash'ari argument.
The objector claims the zahir of the verse supports this interpretation.
4
Analyse the rebuttal using the second verse and taghlib
The Ash'ari response uses the verse 'Inform Me of the names of these' (al-Baqara 31). If 'names' meant realities, then 'names of these' would be redundant (adding a thing to itself). Therefore 'names' must refer to words. The commentator also notes that the plural pronoun in 'then He presented them' is explained via taghlib (inclusion).
This shows that interpretation (ta'wil) is necessary, and the Ash'ari position is defensible.

Source Text

الإفادة، لا أن هذا الوصف ليس ثابتاً بما هو في الضمير (فليس) الوضع (للصورة الذهنية)، فإما للمعاني من حيث هي (أو) الأمر الخارجي كما قيل فقوله : هذا معطوف على المجرور في قوله للمعاني، يعني أن الصورة الذهنية بمراحل عن كونها موضوعاً لها، فهو إما الشيء من حيث هو أو الأمر الخارجي كما قيل وأشار إلى أن الحق هو الأول : فإن كونه في الخارج أيضاً قد لا يراد إفهامه بتة وقيل : النزاع مبني على أن المعلوم هو الصورة الذهنية عند قائلها فتدبر (وقد جعل بعض الأعلام النزاع) الواقع بين أهل هذه المذاهب (لفظياً) وقال من قال إنها موضوعة للصور الذهنية، أراد المعاني من حيث هي، فإن الصورة بما تطلق عليها أيضاً، ومن قال إنها للأمر الخارجي أراد المعاني من حيث كونها متصفة بالوجود الخارجي (ثم الواضع من هو اختلف فيه فقال الأشعري) معرفة الوضع (بالتوقيف الإلهي ، فهو الواضع لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَمَ ءَادَمَ الْأَسْمَاءَ كُلَهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ٣١] فتعليم الأسماء لآدم من الله عز وجل، فليس هو الواضع ولا الملائكة، لأنهم عجزوا عن البيان، واحتمال كون الجنة واضعين أبعد، فالواضع هو الله تعالى، فإن قيل : المراد المسميات، والمعنى علم الله المسميات كلها لآدم بل هو الظاهر، لأن الكمال معرفة الحقائق لا الألفاظ وأوضاعها قال وليس المراد المسميات بدليل) قوله تعالى : ((أَنْبِتُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ ﴾ [البقرة : (۳۱] فإن المسميات هي المشار إليها فحينئذ يلزم إضافة الشيء إلى نفسه (وأول بمسميات الحقائق) فلا يلزم إضافة الشيء إلى نفسه، فالمشار إليه الحقائق، والمضاف المسميات، فإن قلت: هذا تأويل فلا يصار إليه من غير ضرورة ويلزم تأويل آخر في قوله : ثمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى الْمَلَيكَةِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۳۱] قلت : التأويل لازم عليه بحمل قوله تعالى : ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى الْمَلَكَةِ على التغليب والضرورة في هذا التأويل أن لا كمال يعتد به بالنسبة إلى الأنبياء
Then the roots of languages are placed for meanings as such, without consideration of their being in the mind or external, because the placement is for expressing what is in the conscience, i.e., something known intended to be communicated. And its being in the conscience is not in the conscience, i.e., it is not known intended to be communicated, not that this description is not established through being in the conscience. So placement is not for the mental image; rather it is either for meanings as such, or for the external thing as has been said. So his statement is conjoined to the prepositional phrase 'for meanings', meaning that the mental image is far from being the object of placement. So it is either the thing as such or the external thing as has been said. And he indicated that the truth is the first: for its being external also may not be intended to be understood at all. And it was said: the dispute is built on whether the known per se is what is in the conscience or in the external or without consideration of both, and the known per se is the real object of placement. But this statement is devoid of investigation, for no one has held that the known per se is what is in the mental accidents which is the mental image according to its proponent. So reflect. And some scholars considered the dispute between the adherents of these schools as verbal. They said: whoever said that they are placed for mental images intended meanings as such, for 'image' can be applied to them also; and whoever said that they are for the external thing intended meanings as being qualified by external existence. Then, the positor: who is he? There is disagreement. al-Ash'ari said: knowledge of placement is by divine tawqif, so He is the positor, due to His statement: 'And He taught Adam all the names' (al-Baqara 31). So teaching the names to Adam is from Allah, so Adam is not the positor, nor the angels, for they were unable to explain. And the possibility that paradise dwellers are the positors is more remote. So the positor is Allah. If it is said: what is meant is the named entities, and the meaning is that Allah taught Adam all the named entities; indeed it is apparent, because perfection is knowledge of realities, not of words and their placements. He said: by evidence it is not meant the named entities due to His statement: 'Inform Me of the names of these' (al-Baqara 31). For the named entities are what is pointed to, so then adding the thing to itself would be necessary. And he interpreted as [names of] the realities, so adding the thing to itself is not necessary. Then what is pointed to is the realities, and what is added is the names. If you say: this is interpretation, so one should not resort to it without necessity, and another interpretation would be necessary in His statement: 'then He presented them to the angels' (al-Baqara 31). I say: interpretation is necessary for him by carrying His statement 'then He presented them to the angels' as an inclusion (taghlib), and the necessity in this interpretation is that there is no perfection worthy of consideration relative to the prophets.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of wad' (linguistic placement) by first clarifying that the placement is for meanings as such, not for mental images or external objects. It argues against the idea that words are placed for mental images, stating that the mental image is far from being the object of placement. Some scholars considered this dispute verbal: both sides ultimately intend meanings. The main focus then shifts to the identity of the wadi' (the one who places language). The text presents the Ash'ari view that language is from divine tawqif, citing the Quranic verse 'And He taught Adam all the names.' The argument is that since angels could not explain the names, and Adam did not place them himself, the teacher (Allah) is the positor. A potential objection is raised: the verse might mean that Allah taught Adam the named entities (realities) rather than the words. The response uses the subsequent verse 'Inform Me of the names of these' to show that the 'names' must refer to words, not the named things, because otherwise it would be an addition of a thing to itself. The commentator notes that this requires an interpretation, and another verse 'then He presented them to the angels' also needs interpretation via taghlib (inclusion). The text ends abruptly.

Key Terms
الوضع (al-wad'): The act of assigning a word to a meaning; the linguistic convention that establishes a relationship between lafz and ma'na.
التوقيف (al-tawqif): Divine revelation or teaching as the source of linguistic placement.
المسميات (al-musammayat): The named entities or objects themselves, as opposed to the words (asma').
التغليب (al-taghlib): A rhetorical device where one term is used to include another, e.g., presenting 'them' (plural) when the actual entities are mixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari argument presented in the passage, why does the verse 'Inform Me of the names of these' (al-Baqara 31) prove that 'names' refers to words and not to the named entities?
A) Because the named entities are what is being pointed to, so 'names of these' would be addition of a thing to itself if it meant the realities.
B) Because the angels could not understand the realities.
C) Because the verse uses the word 'names' which always means words.
D) Because the verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic proof for divine tawqif hinges on interpreting 'names' as words rather than realities, supported by a second verse that prevents tautology.

The Dispute on the Originator of Language in Usul al-Fiqh
Presenting the Ash'ari, Bahshamiyya, and other views on wadi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key arguments for and against the divine origin of language (tawqif vs. istilah) and evaluate the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Language is divinely revealed (tawqif), not human convention — the wadi' is God.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the classical dispute on the originator of language (wadi' al-lugha). The Ash'ari position (supported by Hanafis) holds that language is established by divine revelation (tawqif), while the Bahshamiyya (Mu'tazila) argue for human convention (istilah). Understanding this dispute is crucial because it affects the epistemological weight of linguistic meanings in textual interpretation (Usul al-Fiqh). We will follow the author's presentation of the proofs and counter-arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main positions
List the three views: tawqif (Ash'ari), istilah (Bahshamiyya), and tawaqquf (suspension of judgment).
2
Examine Al-Ash'ari's primary proof
Analyze Quran 2:31 — 'And He taught Adam all the names'. This indicates that God is the teacher of names, i.e., the wadi'.
The author also addresses objections about 'names' meaning 'named things'.
3
Analyze the Bahshamiyya's counter-proof
Quran 14:4 — 'We sent no messenger except in the language of his people'. They argue language pre-exists the messenger, so it must be conventional.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
God taught language to Adam first, then to each people through their messenger. So language still originates from God.
5
Consider the rational argument of appropriateness
The author argues that there is a natural connection (munasaba) between words and meanings; otherwise assignment would be arbitrary, which is unworthy of God as the wadi'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قبل الرسول وقد تشهد الآية خلافه (وأجيب) بأنا لا نسلم أنه لو كان الواضع هو الله تعالى لكان علمها بالتوقيف من الرسل، كيف وأنه تعالى علمها آدم أولاً قبل الإرسال (ثم اختص كل قوم بلغته فأرسل رسول ذلك القوم
