Distinguishing Ibarah and Isharah in Quran 2:233
Examining Quran 2:233 to illustrate the distinction between ibarah and isharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dalalat al-ibarah and dalalat al-isharah in Quranic verses, and apply the Hanafi usul principles to identify which rulings are derived from each type.

Core Idea
The lam of possession indicates exclusive lineage by ibarah, but derived legal consequences are indicated by isharah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi usul analysis of Quran 2:233. The verse obligates fathers to provide maintenance, but through the wording 'al-mawludu lahu', it also implies the exclusive lineage of the child. The text argues that lineage itself is actually expressed (ibarah), while the subsequent rulings—like eligibility for imamate—are merely implied (isharah). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its explicit ruling
The verse is 2:233, which explicitly obligates maintenance for the mother upon the father. This is the primary purpose (ibarah).
2
Locate the phrase that implies additional meaning
The phrase 'al-mawludu lahu' uses the lam of possession, implying that the child belongs exclusively to the father in lineage.
The lam is a particle of possession.
3
Classify the type of indication for lineage
According to the Hanafi author, this indication is ibarah, not isharah, because the lam is placed for exclusivity and that meaning is intentionally conveyed, even though the primary intent is maintenance.
The author says 'al-dalalatu 'alayhi 'ibaratun la isharah'.
4
Identify rulings that are genuinely isharah
Rulings like eligibility for imamate and kafa'ah (compatibility) are derived from lineage but are not directly expressed; they are indicated by isharah.
These follow necessarily from the establishment of lineage.
5
Apply the distinction to other verses
When studying any verse, first identify what is explicitly stated (ibarah) and then what is secondarily implied (isharah), noting that only truly non-intended consequences are isharah.
The same method can be applied to other Quranic texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون خفياً فدلالته خفية فقد تكون نظرية ) لخفاء اللزوم (كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوف [البقرة: ۲۳۳] (الآية) فهي لإيجاب النفقة على الآباء ولكن قد عبر سبحانه عنهم بالمولود له، ونسب الولد إليهم بحرف اللام ففيه إشارة إلى اختصاص الولد بالوالد نسباً) إذ لم يرد التمليك قطعاً فينفرد بنفقته ولا يجب شيء منها على الأم (ويستتبعه) هذا الولد بأهلية الإمامة الكبرى التي هي السلطنة العامة فيستحقه إن كان الأب قرشياً (والكفاءة) فيصير كفؤا لمن أبوه كفء له إلا الحرية والرق فإنه لا يكون حراً وموقوفاً بحرية الأب ورقه (بدليل) خاص بهما وغير ذلك من الأحكام المتعلقة كالعقل وغيره، ثم في كون الدلالة على اختصاص الولد بالوالد من الإشارة نظر فإن اللام موضوع للاختصاص، وقد أريد ههنا الاختصاص الخاص، فالمراد بالمولود له من انتسب إليه الولد وهذا المعنى هو المقصود وإن كان القصد إليه لإيجاب النفقة عليه، فالدلالة عليه عبارة لا إشارة نعم الدلالة على ترتب الأحكام المذكورة على ثبوت النسب إشارة البتة فافهم (وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ الَّذِينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَارِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ۸] الآية فإنه وإن سيق لإيجاب سهم الغنيمة لهم (دل على زوال الملك عما خلفوا لأن الفقير من لا يملك شيئاً من المال، ففي التعبير عنهم بالفقير إشارة إلى زوال الملك، وإلا صاروا أغنياء (لا يقال لفظ الفقير (استعارة لإضافة الأموال إليهم) فيكونون ملاك الأموال، فلا يكونون فقراء ، بل استعير لمن انقطع طمعه عن الانتفاع بالمال لأن الإضافة الدالة على الملك حين (الإخراج من الديار والأموال (لا تنافي الفقر (الآن) فلا تصلح الإضافة قرينة على ثبوت الاستعارة فيترك الفقير على الحقيقة (و) قال (في «التحرير» : والوجه أنه أي زوال الملك بل الدلالة عليه (اقتضاء لأن صحة إطلاق الفقير بعد ثبوت ملك) الفقير الأموال) متوقفة على الزوال فيكون الزوال لازماً متقدماً والدلالة عليه اقتضاء (أقول) إطلاق الفقراء وإن توقف على زوال الملك، لكن لا يتوقف على الزوال بالاستيلاء، فكون الاستيلاء مزيلا) ملك المؤمنين (موجباً للملك لهم أي للمستولين الكفار (ثابت بالإشارة عن كما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: ﴿أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَرِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ٨] لأن التعليق بالمشتق يوجب عليه المبدأ فالإخراج سبب الفقر فتدبر) وهذا غير وافٍ فإن كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً وموجباً حكم، ونفس زوال الملك حكم آخر، وصاحب التحرير إنما حكم على الثاني بكونه اقتضاء دون الأوّل فتدبر ؛ فالأولى في الجواب ما قاله مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره إن توقف الإطلاق على أمر لا يوجب كونه اقتضاء ، وإلا لزم أن يكون جميع اللوازم اقتضاء لتوقف الإطلاق عليها البتة بل الاقتضاء الدلالة على أمر يتوقف عليه صحة المعنى المفهوم، وليس ههنا كذلك فإن زوال الملك والفقر معان من غير توقف لأحدهما على الآخر فلم تكن إلا إشارة هذا وبعد بقي في الكلام كلام فإنه يدل الفقير مطابقة على من لا يملك شيئاً، فكون المهاجرين رضوان الله تعالى عليهم غير مالكي ما خلفوا مقصوده في الجملة، وإن لم يكن مقصوداً بالذات فهو عبارة ؛ نعم الدلالة على كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً موجباً غير مقصود إشارة فافهم (وكقوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ هُنَّ لِبَاسٌ لَكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ لِبَاسٌ لَّهُنَّ عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَعَفَا عَنكُمْ فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ وَابْتَغُوا مَا كَتَبَ اللهُ لَكُمْ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى الَّيْلِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] (دل) هذا القول على جواز الإصباح جنباً) للصائم، لا كما يقوله الروافض خذلهم الله تعالى : من أصبح جنباً فقد أفطر وتقريره على ما هو المشهور أن الغاية دلت على جواز الاستمتاع بهنّ إلى الفجر فجاز الاستمتاع في آخر أجزاء الليل، وهو يستلزم كونه جنباً في أول أجزاء الفجر، وأورد عليه أن حتى غاية للأكل والشرب، فيجوزان في آخر أجزاء الليل لا الاستمتاع بالنساء، وأجيب بأن حتى غاية لقوله: ﴿فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] إلى الآخر بدلالة السياق، فإن الآية في نفي حرمة الاستمتاع والأكل والشرب، من بعد ثلث الليل، فأبيح الأشياء الثلاثة إلى الفجر، ولو سلمنا وتنزلنا فالاستمتاع مثل الأكل والشرب، فإذا جازا إلى آخر الليل جاز أيضاً بمفهومه الموافق، لكن على هذا كونه من باب الإشارة غير ظاهر، وسلك المصنف مسلكاً آخر هو أن قوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] دل بعبارته على حل الاستمتاع بهن في الليل كله فلزم الإصباح جنباً (فإنه لازم من استغراق الليل بالرفث قطعاً) وعلى هذا لا شائبة للإيراد عليه أصلاً (قيل : اللازم) الآية (جواز الوقاع في جزء منه لا في جميعه) فإن ليلة الرفث مطلقة (أقول: قد في للاستيعاب فدل الآية على استغراق حل الرفث بالليل على أنه نسخ للحظر، المتعلق بالجميع كما روى أبو داود والبيهقي عن ابن عباس في : ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۳] قال : فكان الناس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم إذا صلوا العتمة حرم عليهم الطعام والشراب والنساء وصاموا إلى القابلة فاختان رجل نفسه فجامع امرأته وقد صلّى العشاء ولم يفطر، فأراد الله أن يجعل ذلك يسراً لمن بقي ورخصة ومنفعة فقال : ﴿عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] الآية فرخص لهم ويسر وفي رواية البخاري وأبي داود والترمذي عن البراء بن عازب قال : كان أصحاب النبي إذا كان الرجل صائماً فحضر الإفطار فنام قبل أن يفطر لم يأكل ليلته ولا يومه حتى يمسي، وأن قيس بن صرمة الأنصاري كان صائماً، وكان يومه يعمل في أرضه، فلما حضر الإفطار أتى امرأته فقال : هل عندك طعام؟ قالت : لا ولكن أنطلق فأطلب لك، فغلبته عينه فنام وجاءته امرأته فلما رأته نائماً قالت : خيبة لك أنمت فلما انتصف النهار غشي عليه فذكر ذلك للنبي فأنزلت هذه الآية أحل لكم ليلة الصيام الرفث إلى قوله : من الفجر، ففرحوا بها فرحاً شديداً وفي الروايتين نحو من التعارض، ولفظ الآية يؤيد الأولى، وعلى كل تقدير فالآية ناسخة للتحريم المستغرق جميع الليلة (فيجوز) في جميع الليل (كما كان محرماً فيها، لأن ارتفاع الحظر يلزمه الإباحة إلى أن يقوم الدليل على التحريم وليس فافهم، ثم لو تنزلنا وسلمنا أن ليلة الصيام مطلقة لم يضرنا فإنه حينئذ يدل على جواز المس في كل جزء من أجزاء الليل ومنه الأخير فلزم جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً فافهم، واعلم أن جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً ثابت بدلائل لا شبهة فيه منها ما أخرج الشيخان ومالك وابن أبي
[The passage discusses types of indication (dalalah). It begins:] It may be hidden, so its indication is hidden, and it may be theoretical due to the hiddenness of the implication. Like His statement, Exalted is He: {And upon the father [of the child] is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable} (2:233) — this verse is for obligating maintenance upon fathers, but He, Glorified, expressed them as 'the one to whom the child is born', and attributed the child to them with the letter lam, so in it there is an indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father in lineage, since possession is definitely not intended. So he alone is liable for his maintenance, and nothing is obligatory upon the mother. And this entails for this child the eligibility for the greater imamate, which is general sovereignty, so he deserves it if the father is Qurayshi, and [entails] compatibility (kafa'ah), so he becomes compatible for one whose father is compatible for him, except for freedom and slavery, for he is not free and suspended by the father's freedom or slavery, by a specific proof for both, and other related rulings like reason and others. Then, regarding the indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father being from isharah (implication), there is consideration, for the lam is placed for exclusivity, and here the specific exclusivity is intended. So what is meant by 'the one to whom the child is born' is one to whom the child is attributed, and this meaning is the intended one, even if the purpose towards it is for obligating maintenance upon him. So the indication upon it is ibarah (explicit expression), not isharah. Yes, the indication of the arrangement of the mentioned rulings upon the establishment of lineage is definitely isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties} (59:8) — although it was put forward to obligate the share of war booty for them, it indicates the removal of ownership over what they left behind, because the poor person is one who does not possess any wealth. So in describing them as poor, there is an indication of removal of ownership; otherwise they would become rich. It cannot be said that the word 'poor' is a metaphor due to the addition of wealth to them, so they would be owners of wealth and thus not poor. Rather, it is used metaphorically for one whose hope for benefiting from wealth is cut off, because the addition indicating ownership at the time of expulsion from homes and properties does not negate poverty now, so the addition does not serve as evidence for the establishment of metaphor, so 'poor' is left on its literal meaning. And the author of al-Tahrir said: The correct view is that it, i.e., the removal of ownership, or rather the indication upon it, is iqtida' (necessary implication), because the validity of applying 'poor' after the establishment of ownership of wealth is dependent on removal, so removal is necessary and prior, and the indication upon it is iqtida'. I say: The application of 'poor' although dependent on removal of ownership, is not dependent on removal by usurpation. So that usurpation is a remove of the ownership of the believers and a cause of ownership for them, i.e., for the disbeliever usurpers, is established by isharah, just as His statement points to it: {expelled from their homes and their properties} because attribution by the derived term necessitates the basis, so expulsion is the cause of poverty, so ponder. But this is insufficient, for that usurpation is a remover and a cause is a ruling, and the very removal of ownership is another ruling. The author of al-Tahrir only ruled on the second as being iqtida', not the first, so ponder. So the best answer is what the revealer of divine secrets, may Allah sanctify his secret, said: That the dependence of the application on something does not necessitate it being iqtida', otherwise all necessary concomitants would be iqtida' due to the application's absolute dependence on them. Rather, iqtida' is the indication of something on which the correctness of the understood meaning depends. And it is not like that here, for removal of ownership and poverty are meanings with no dependence of one on the other, so it was nothing but isharah. After this, there remains discussion in the speech, for 'poor' literally indicates one who possesses nothing. So that the emigrants, may Allah be pleased with them, are not owners of what they left behind is intended in general, and if not intended per se, it is ibarah. Yes, the indication that usurpation is a remover and a cause is unintended isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women. They are garments for you and you are garments for them. Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves, so He relented towards you and pardoned you. So now have relations with them and seek what Allah has written for you, and eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn. Then complete the fast until the night} (2:187). This verse indicates the permissibility of becoming junub (in a state of major ritual impurity) at dawn for the fasting person, not as the rejected Rafidah say: 'Whoever becomes junub at dawn has broken his fast.' The explanation, according to what is well-known, is that the limit (ghayah) indicated the permissibility of enjoying them until dawn, so enjoyment is permissible in the last parts of the night, which entails being junub in the first parts of dawn. An objection was raised that 'until' is a limit for eating and drinking, so they are permissible in the last parts of the night, not the enjoyment of women. The answer is that 'until' is a limit for His statement {so now have relations with them} to the end, by implication of context, for the verse is about negating the prohibition of enjoyment, eating, and drinking after one third of the night, so the three things were permitted until dawn. Even if we concede and assume, enjoyment is like eating and drinking, so if they are permissible until the end of the night, it is also permissible by its parallel meaning (mafhum muwafaqah). But on this, its being from the category of isharah is not apparent. The author took another path: that His statement {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women} explicitly indicates the permissibility of enjoying them throughout the whole night, so becoming junub at dawn is necessary, for it is a necessary consequence of spending the whole night in relations. And on this, there is no trace of objection at all. It was said: What is necessitated by the verse is the permissibility of intercourse in a part of it, not all of it, for 'the night of relations' is unrestricted. I say: The letter 'lam' in 'li-laylati' is for istighraq (comprehensiveness), so the verse indicates the permissibility of relations throughout the night, and it abrogated the prohibition that pertained to the whole night, as narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas regarding {O you who believe, fasting is prescribed for you...} (2:183). He said: People at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family, when they prayed the night prayer, food, drink, and women became forbidden to them, and they fasted until the next night. So a man betrayed himself and had intercourse with his wife after having prayed the night prayer and not broken his fast. Allah wanted to make that easy for those who remained, a concession and benefit, so He said: {Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves...} and the verse, so He granted them concession and made things easy. In another narration by al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: The Companions of the Prophet, when a man was fasting and the time of breaking fast came, if he slept before breaking fast, he would not eat that night nor the next day until evening. And Qays ibn Sirmah al-Ansari was fasting, and he was working in his land that day. When the time of breaking fast came, he went to his wife and said: Do you have food? She said: No, but I will go and seek for you. So sleep overcame him and he slept. His wife came and when she saw him sleeping, she said: Disappointment for you! You slept. When midday came, he lost consciousness. That was mentioned to the Prophet, so this verse was revealed: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations...} up to His saying 'from the dawn'. They rejoiced greatly at it. The two narrations are somewhat contradictory, and the wording of the verse supports the first. In any case, the verse abrogates the prohibition that covered the entire night, so it is permissible throughout the whole night, just as it was prohibited in it, because the removal of prohibition necessitates permissibility until evidence for prohibition comes, and there is none, so understand. Then even if we concede and accept that 'the night of fasting' is unrestricted, it does not harm us, for then it indicates the permissibility of intercourse in every part of the night, including the last, so the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is necessitated, so understand. And know that the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is established by proofs with no doubt, including what al-Bukhari, Muslim, Malik, and Ibn Abi...
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the various types of textual indication (dalalah) in Quranic verses, specifically focusing on 'dalalat al-isharah' (indication by implication) as opposed to 'dalalat al-ibarah' (explicit indication). The author, commenting on 'Muslim al-Thubut', uses three examples to illustrate how verses can imply rulings beyond their immediate explicit meaning. 

The first example is Quran 2:233 concerning maintenance of children. The verse explicitly obligates the father to provide for his child's mother, but through the phrase 'al-mawludu lahu' (the one to whom the child is born) and the use of the possessive 'lam', it implies the exclusive lineage of the child to the father. The author then explains that this exclusivity is actually a clear expression (ibarah) of lineage, not merely an implication (isharah). However, the subsequent rulings—such as eligibility for imamate, compatibility in marriage, and other legal consequences—are indeed derived through isharah from the establishment of lineage. This nuanced distinction shows the careful application of usul terminology.

The second example is Quran 59:8 referring to the poor emigrants. The verse is primarily for allocating the spoils to them, but describing them as 'poor' implies that they lost ownership of the property they left behind. The author discusses an objection that 'poor' might be metaphorical, since they still had ownership at the time of expulsion. The response clarifies that the description is literal because ownership was removed, and the indication of removal is isharah. The author then engages with the view of 'al-Tahrir' that this is iqtida' (necessary implication) and refines the analysis, concluding that it is isharah.

The third and most extensive example is Quran 2:187, which permits marital relations during Ramadan nights. This verse implicitly indicates that a fasting person may be in a state of janabah (major impurity) at dawn, contrary to the Rafidah view. The author presents several arguments: (1) The limit (ghayah) 'until dawn' applies to all permitted activities—eating, drinking, and relations—so engaging in relations in the last part of the night leads to janabah at dawn. (2) Even if 'until' only applies to eating and drinking, the same permissibility for relations is derived by qiyas or mafhum muwafaqah. (3) The author's preferred argument is that the verse literally permits relations throughout the whole night (istighraq), so janabah at dawn is a necessary consequence. He supports this with narrations about the abrogation of a prior stricter rule that prohibited any activity after evening prayer. The passage concludes by asserting that the permissibility is well-established with clear proofs.

Key Terms
دلالة الإشارة (dalālat al-ishārah): Indication by implication: where the text implies a meaning that is not the primary intended meaning but follows from it necessarily or by context.
دلالة العبارة (dalālat al-‘ibārah): Explicit indication: where the text directly expresses the intended meaning without need for inference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis of Quran 2:233, which of the following is indicated by isharah?
A) The father's obligation to provide maintenance.
B) The child's exclusive lineage to the father.
C) The child's eligibility for the greater imamate.
D) The use of the lam as a possessive particle.

Key Takeaway
The lam of possession in Quran 2:233 indicates exclusive lineage by ibarah, while subsequent legal consequences are indicated by isharah.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
9 min
Dalalat al-Isharah in Quran 59:8: Removal of Ownership
Examining Quran 59:8 to distinguish isharah from iqtida'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Quran 59:8 indicates the removal of ownership from the emigrants through dalalat al-isharah, and differentiate between isharah and iqtida' in this context.

Core Idea
Describing the emigrants as 'poor' implies loss of ownership; this is isharah, not iqtida' or ibarah.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi usul analysis of Quran 59:8. The verse describes the emigrants as 'poor' to allocate the spoils to them, but it also implies that they lost ownership of what they left behind. The text engages in a debate over whether this indication is isharah or iqtida' (necessary implication), ultimately concluding it is isharah. Understanding this requires applying the usul test: does the correctness of the statement depend on the implied meaning?

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its explicit purpose
Quran 59:8 is primarily for obligating a share of the spoils to the poor emigrants. The explicit ruling is the allocation of war booty.
2
Analyze the description 'poor'
Calling them 'poor' (fuqara') indicates they do not possess wealth. This implies that they lost ownership of the property they left behind in Mecca.
The literal meaning of 'faqir' is one who owns nothing.
3
Examine the claim that this is iqtida'
Some argue that the validity of calling them poor after they had wealth depends on the removal of ownership, so the removal is iqtida' (necessary for correctness). The author of al-Tahrir supported this.
Iqtida' is when the implied meaning is required for the text to be true.
4
Refute the iqtida' claim
The author argues that the application of 'poor' does not depend on removal by usurpation; it simply states their state at the time of the verse. The removal of ownership and poverty are independent concepts, so it is isharah, not iqtida'.
The dependence must be for the correctness of the understood meaning, which is not the case here.
5
Conclude the type of indication
The indication of removal of ownership is isharah. Additionally, the indication that usurpation causes removal and transfer of ownership is also isharah, as it is not directly intended.
The author notes that the verse's wording 'expelled from their homes and properties' supports this by pointing to the cause of poverty.

مِن دِيَارِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ۸] الآية فإنه وإن سيق لإيجاب سهم الغنيمة لهم (دل على زوال الملك عما خلفوا لأن الفقير من لا يملك شيئاً من المال، ففي التعبير عنهم بالفقير إشارة إلى زوال الملك، وإلا صاروا أغنياء (لا يقال لفظ الفقير (استعارة لإضافة الأموال إليهم) فيكونون ملاك الأموال، فلا يكونون فقراء ، بل استعير لمن انقطع طمعه عن الانتفاع بالمال لأن الإضافة الدالة على الملك حين (الإخراج من الديار والأموال (لا تنافي الفقر (الآن) فلا تصلح الإضافة قرينة على ثبوت الاستعارة فيترك الفقير على الحقيقة (و) قال (في «التحرير» : والوجه أنه أي زوال الملك بل الدلالة عليه (اقتضاء لأن صحة إطلاق الفقير بعد ثبوت ملك) الفقير الأموال) متوقفة على الزوال فيكون الزوال لازماً متقدماً والدلالة عليه اقتضاء (أقول) إطلاق الفقراء وإن توقف على زوال الملك، لكن لا يتوقف على الزوال بالاستيلاء، فكون الاستيلاء مزيلا) ملك المؤمنين (موجباً للملك لهم أي للمستولين الكفار (ثابت بالإشارة عن كما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: ﴿أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَرِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ٨] لأن التعليق بالمشتق يوجب عليه المبدأ فالإخراج سبب الفقر فتدبر) وهذا غير وافٍ فإن كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً وموجباً حكم، ونفس زوال الملك حكم آخر، وصاحب التحرير إنما حكم على الثاني بكونه اقتضاء دون الأوّل فتدبر ؛ فالأولى في الجواب ما قاله مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره إن توقف الإطلاق على أمر لا يوجب كونه اقتضاء ، وإلا لزم أن يكون جميع اللوازم اقتضاء لتوقف الإطلاق عليها البتة بل الاقتضاء الدلالة على أمر يتوقف عليه صحة المعنى المفهوم، وليس ههنا كذلك فإن زوال الملك والفقر معان من غير توقف لأحدهما على الآخر فلم تكن إلا إشارة هذا وبعد بقي في الكلام كلام فإنه يدل الفقير مطابقة على من لا يملك شيئاً، فكون المهاجرين رضوان الله تعالى عليهم غير مالكي ما خلفوا مقصوده في الجملة، وإن لم يكن مقصوداً بالذات فهو عبارة ؛ نعم الدلالة على كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً موجباً غير مقصود إشارة فافهم (وكقوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ هُنَّ لِبَاسٌ لَكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ لِبَاسٌ لَّهُنَّ عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَعَفَا عَنكُمْ فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ وَابْتَغُوا مَا كَتَبَ اللهُ لَكُمْ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى الَّيْلِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] (دل) هذا القول على جواز الإصباح جنباً) للصائم، لا كما يقوله الروافض خذلهم الله تعالى : من أصبح جنباً فقد أفطر وتقريره على ما هو المشهور أن الغاية دلت على جواز الاستمتاع بهنّ إلى الفجر فجاز الاستمتاع في آخر أجزاء الليل، وهو يستلزم كونه جنباً في أول أجزاء الفجر، وأورد عليه أن حتى غاية للأكل والشرب، فيجوزان في آخر أجزاء الليل لا الاستمتاع بالنساء، وأجيب بأن حتى غاية لقوله: ﴿فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] إلى الآخر بدلالة السياق، فإن الآية في نفي حرمة الاستمتاع والأكل والشرب، من بعد ثلث الليل، فأبيح الأشياء الثلاثة إلى الفجر، ولو سلمنا وتنزلنا فالاستمتاع مثل الأكل والشرب، فإذا جازا إلى آخر الليل جاز أيضاً بمفهومه الموافق، لكن على هذا كونه من باب الإشارة غير ظاهر، وسلك المصنف مسلكاً آخر هو أن قوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] دل بعبارته على حل الاستمتاع بهن في الليل كله فلزم الإصباح جنباً (فإنه لازم من استغراق الليل بالرفث قطعاً) وعلى هذا لا شائبة للإيراد عليه أصلاً (قيل : اللازم) الآية (جواز الوقاع في جزء منه لا في جميعه) فإن ليلة الرفث مطلقة (أقول: قد في للاستيعاب فدل الآية على استغراق حل الرفث بالليل على أنه نسخ للحظر، المتعلق بالجميع كما روى أبو داود والبيهقي عن ابن عباس في : ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۳] قال : فكان الناس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم إذا صلوا العتمة حرم عليهم الطعام والشراب والنساء وصاموا إلى القابلة فاختان رجل نفسه فجامع امرأته وقد صلّى العشاء ولم يفطر، فأراد الله أن يجعل ذلك يسراً لمن بقي ورخصة ومنفعة فقال : ﴿عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] الآية فرخص لهم ويسر وفي رواية البخاري وأبي داود والترمذي عن البراء بن عازب قال : كان أصحاب النبي إذا كان الرجل صائماً فحضر الإفطار فنام قبل أن يفطر لم يأكل ليلته ولا يومه حتى يمسي، وأن قيس بن صرمة الأنصاري كان صائماً، وكان يومه يعمل في أرضه، فلما حضر الإفطار أتى امرأته فقال : هل عندك طعام؟ قالت : لا ولكن أنطلق فأطلب لك، فغلبته عينه فنام وجاءته امرأته فلما رأته نائماً قالت : خيبة لك أنمت فلما انتصف النهار غشي عليه فذكر ذلك للنبي فأنزلت هذه الآية أحل لكم ليلة الصيام الرفث إلى قوله : من الفجر، ففرحوا بها فرحاً شديداً وفي الروايتين نحو من التعارض، ولفظ الآية يؤيد الأولى، وعلى كل تقدير فالآية ناسخة للتحريم المستغرق جميع الليلة (فيجوز) في جميع الليل (كما كان محرماً فيها، لأن ارتفاع الحظر يلزمه الإباحة إلى أن يقوم الدليل على التحريم وليس فافهم، ثم لو تنزلنا وسلمنا أن ليلة الصيام مطلقة لم يضرنا فإنه حينئذ يدل على جواز المس في كل جزء من أجزاء الليل ومنه الأخير فلزم جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً فافهم، واعلم أن جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً ثابت بدلائل لا شبهة فيه منها ما أخرج الشيخان ومالك وابن أبي
[The passage discusses types of indication (dalalah). It begins:] It may be hidden, so its indication is hidden, and it may be theoretical due to the hiddenness of the implication. Like His statement, Exalted is He: {And upon the father [of the child] is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable} (2:233) — this verse is for obligating maintenance upon fathers, but He, Glorified, expressed them as 'the one to whom the child is born', and attributed the child to them with the letter lam, so in it there is an indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father in lineage, since possession is definitely not intended. So he alone is liable for his maintenance, and nothing is obligatory upon the mother. And this entails for this child the eligibility for the greater imamate, which is general sovereignty, so he deserves it if the father is Qurayshi, and [entails] compatibility (kafa'ah), so he becomes compatible for one whose father is compatible for him, except for freedom and slavery, for he is not free and suspended by the father's freedom or slavery, by a specific proof for both, and other related rulings like reason and others. Then, regarding the indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father being from isharah (implication), there is consideration, for the lam is placed for exclusivity, and here the specific exclusivity is intended. So what is meant by 'the one to whom the child is born' is one to whom the child is attributed, and this meaning is the intended one, even if the purpose towards it is for obligating maintenance upon him. So the indication upon it is ibarah (explicit expression), not isharah. Yes, the indication of the arrangement of the mentioned rulings upon the establishment of lineage is definitely isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties} (59:8) — although it was put forward to obligate the share of war booty for them, it indicates the removal of ownership over what they left behind, because the poor person is one who does not possess any wealth. So in describing them as poor, there is an indication of removal of ownership; otherwise they would become rich. It cannot be said that the word 'poor' is a metaphor due to the addition of wealth to them, so they would be owners of wealth and thus not poor. Rather, it is used metaphorically for one whose hope for benefiting from wealth is cut off, because the addition indicating ownership at the time of expulsion from homes and properties does not negate poverty now, so the addition does not serve as evidence for the establishment of metaphor, so 'poor' is left on its literal meaning. And the author of al-Tahrir said: The correct view is that it, i.e., the removal of ownership, or rather the indication upon it, is iqtida' (necessary implication), because the validity of applying 'poor' after the establishment of ownership of wealth is dependent on removal, so removal is necessary and prior, and the indication upon it is iqtida'. I say: The application of 'poor' although dependent on removal of ownership, is not dependent on removal by usurpation. So that usurpation is a remove of the ownership of the believers and a cause of ownership for them, i.e., for the disbeliever usurpers, is established by isharah, just as His statement points to it: {expelled from their homes and their properties} because attribution by the derived term necessitates the basis, so expulsion is the cause of poverty, so ponder. But this is insufficient, for that usurpation is a remover and a cause is a ruling, and the very removal of ownership is another ruling. The author of al-Tahrir only ruled on the second as being iqtida', not the first, so ponder. So the best answer is what the revealer of divine secrets, may Allah sanctify his secret, said: That the dependence of the application on something does not necessitate it being iqtida', otherwise all necessary concomitants would be iqtida' due to the application's absolute dependence on them. Rather, iqtida' is the indication of something on which the correctness of the understood meaning depends. And it is not like that here, for removal of ownership and poverty are meanings with no dependence of one on the other, so it was nothing but isharah. After this, there remains discussion in the speech, for 'poor' literally indicates one who possesses nothing. So that the emigrants, may Allah be pleased with them, are not owners of what they left behind is intended in general, and if not intended per se, it is ibarah. Yes, the indication that usurpation is a remover and a cause is unintended isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women. They are garments for you and you are garments for them. Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves, so He relented towards you and pardoned you. So now have relations with them and seek what Allah has written for you, and eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn. Then complete the fast until the night} (2:187). This verse indicates the permissibility of becoming junub (in a state of major ritual impurity) at dawn for the fasting person, not as the rejected Rafidah say: 'Whoever becomes junub at dawn has broken his fast.' The explanation, according to what is well-known, is that the limit (ghayah) indicated the permissibility of enjoying them until dawn, so enjoyment is permissible in the last parts of the night, which entails being junub in the first parts of dawn. An objection was raised that 'until' is a limit for eating and drinking, so they are permissible in the last parts of the night, not the enjoyment of women. The answer is that 'until' is a limit for His statement {so now have relations with them} to the end, by implication of context, for the verse is about negating the prohibition of enjoyment, eating, and drinking after one third of the night, so the three things were permitted until dawn. Even if we concede and assume, enjoyment is like eating and drinking, so if they are permissible until the end of the night, it is also permissible by its parallel meaning (mafhum muwafaqah). But on this, its being from the category of isharah is not apparent. The author took another path: that His statement {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women} explicitly indicates the permissibility of enjoying them throughout the whole night, so becoming junub at dawn is necessary, for it is a necessary consequence of spending the whole night in relations. And on this, there is no trace of objection at all. It was said: What is necessitated by the verse is the permissibility of intercourse in a part of it, not all of it, for 'the night of relations' is unrestricted. I say: The letter 'lam' in 'li-laylati' is for istighraq (comprehensiveness), so the verse indicates the permissibility of relations throughout the night, and it abrogated the prohibition that pertained to the whole night, as narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas regarding {O you who believe, fasting is prescribed for you...} (2:183). He said: People at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family, when they prayed the night prayer, food, drink, and women became forbidden to them, and they fasted until the next night. So a man betrayed himself and had intercourse with his wife after having prayed the night prayer and not broken his fast. Allah wanted to make that easy for those who remained, a concession and benefit, so He said: {Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves...} and the verse, so He granted them concession and made things easy. In another narration by al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: The Companions of the Prophet, when a man was fasting and the time of breaking fast came, if he slept before breaking fast, he would not eat that night nor the next day until evening. And Qays ibn Sirmah al-Ansari was fasting, and he was working in his land that day. When the time of breaking fast came, he went to his wife and said: Do you have food? She said: No, but I will go and seek for you. So sleep overcame him and he slept. His wife came and when she saw him sleeping, she said: Disappointment for you! You slept. When midday came, he lost consciousness. That was mentioned to the Prophet, so this verse was revealed: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations...} up to His saying 'from the dawn'. They rejoiced greatly at it. The two narrations are somewhat contradictory, and the wording of the verse supports the first. In any case, the verse abrogates the prohibition that covered the entire night, so it is permissible throughout the whole night, just as it was prohibited in it, because the removal of prohibition necessitates permissibility until evidence for prohibition comes, and there is none, so understand. Then even if we concede and accept that 'the night of fasting' is unrestricted, it does not harm us, for then it indicates the permissibility of intercourse in every part of the night, including the last, so the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is necessitated, so understand. And know that the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is established by proofs with no doubt, including what al-Bukhari, Muslim, Malik, and Ibn Abi...
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the various types of textual indication (dalalah) in Quranic verses, specifically focusing on 'dalalat al-isharah' (indication by implication) as opposed to 'dalalat al-ibarah' (explicit indication). The author, commenting on 'Muslim al-Thubut', uses three examples to illustrate how verses can imply rulings beyond their immediate explicit meaning. 

The first example is Quran 2:233 concerning maintenance of children. The verse explicitly obligates the father to provide for his child's mother, but through the phrase 'al-mawludu lahu' (the one to whom the child is born) and the use of the possessive 'lam', it implies the exclusive lineage of the child to the father. The author then explains that this exclusivity is actually a clear expression (ibarah) of lineage, not merely an implication (isharah). However, the subsequent rulings—such as eligibility for imamate, compatibility in marriage, and other legal consequences—are indeed derived through isharah from the establishment of lineage. This nuanced distinction shows the careful application of usul terminology.

The second example is Quran 59:8 referring to the poor emigrants. The verse is primarily for allocating the spoils to them, but describing them as 'poor' implies that they lost ownership of the property they left behind. The author discusses an objection that 'poor' might be metaphorical, since they still had ownership at the time of expulsion. The response clarifies that the description is literal because ownership was removed, and the indication of removal is isharah. The author then engages with the view of 'al-Tahrir' that this is iqtida' (necessary implication) and refines the analysis, concluding that it is isharah.

The third and most extensive example is Quran 2:187, which permits marital relations during Ramadan nights. This verse implicitly indicates that a fasting person may be in a state of janabah (major impurity) at dawn, contrary to the Rafidah view. The author presents several arguments: (1) The limit (ghayah) 'until dawn' applies to all permitted activities—eating, drinking, and relations—so engaging in relations in the last part of the night leads to janabah at dawn. (2) Even if 'until' only applies to eating and drinking, the same permissibility for relations is derived by qiyas or mafhum muwafaqah. (3) The author's preferred argument is that the verse literally permits relations throughout the whole night (istighraq), so janabah at dawn is a necessary consequence. He supports this with narrations about the abrogation of a prior stricter rule that prohibited any activity after evening prayer. The passage concludes by asserting that the permissibility is well-established with clear proofs.

Key Terms
دلالة الإشارة (dalālat al-ishārah): Indication by implication: where the text implies a meaning that is not the primary intended meaning but follows from it necessarily or by context.
اقتضاء (iqtidā’): Necessary implication: where a meaning is necessarily required for the validity of the explicit text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis of Quran 59:8, what type of indication does the description 'poor' have regarding the removal of ownership?
A) Iqtida' because the verse would be false if they still owned property.
B) Isharah because it is a necessary consequence, not a requirement for truth.
C) Ibarah because the verse explicitly states they lost ownership.
D) Mafhum mukhalafah because the opposite is not mentioned.

Key Takeaway
In Quran 59:8, the indication that the emigrants lost ownership is isharah, not iqtida', because the truth of the description 'poor' does not depend on the removal itself.

Dalalat al-Isharah in Quran 2:187: Permissibility of Janabah at Dawn for the Fasting Person
Examining Quran 2:187 to derive the permissibility of janabah at dawn for the fasting person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Quran 2:187 indicates, through dalalat al-isharah, that it is permissible for a fasting person to be in a state of janabah (major impurity) at dawn, and contrast the Hanafi position with that of the Rafidah.

Core Idea
The verse's permission of relations throughout the night necessarily implies permissibility of janabah at dawn for the fasting person.

This lesson examines the Hanafi usal derivation from Quran 2:187. The verse permits marital relations during Ramadan nights, ending at dawn. The logical consequence is that a fasting person may be in a state of janabah at the start of the fast. The text presents several arguments, including that the limit (ghayah) applies to all permitted acts and that the verse abrogated an earlier prohibition. This leads to a dispute with the Rafidah, who consider janabah at dawn invalidates the fast. Understanding this derivation involves applying the principles of istighraq (comprehensiveness), abrogation (naskh), and necessary implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its context
Quran 2:187 permits eating, drinking, and marital relations during Ramadan nights until dawn. The verse was revealed to abrogate a stricter rule that prohibited all contact after the night prayer.
2
Understand the main argument for janabah at dawn
Since relations are permitted until dawn (the limit), engaging in them in the last moment of the night necessarily leads to being junub at dawn. This is a necessary consequence (isharah).
The author uses the istighraq of the night by the lam and the abrogation to support permissibility for the whole night.
3
Address the objection that 'until' only applies to eating and drinking
The response is that the limit applies to all three activities due to the context of the verse, which is to lift the earlier total prohibition.
Even if it only applied to eating/drinking, relations are analogous (qiyas) to them, so they are also permitted until dawn.
4
Consider the Rafidah opposing view
The Rafidah claim that becoming junub at dawn invalidates the fast. The Hanafi response relies on the clear implication of the verse and the abrogation of the earlier prohibition.
The Rafidah interpret the verse differently or rely on other evidence.
5
Recognize the type of dalalah
The permissibility of janabah at dawn is indicated by isharah because it is a necessary consequence of the explicit permission of relations throughout the night. It is not directly stated.
The author also mentions that this ruling is confirmed by multiple proofs (hadith).

سبحانه عنهم بالمولود له، ونسب الولد إليهم بحرف اللام ففيه إشارة إلى اختصاص الولد بالوالد نسباً) إذ لم يرد التمليك قطعاً فينفرد بنفقته ولا يجب شيء منها على الأم (ويستتبعه) هذا الولد بأهلية الإمامة الكبرى التي هي السلطنة العامة فيستحقه إن كان الأب قرشياً (والكفاءة) فيصير كفؤا لمن أبوه كفء له إلا الحرية والرق فإنه لا يكون حراً وموقوفاً بحرية الأب ورقه (بدليل) خاص بهما وغير ذلك من الأحكام المتعلقة كالعقل وغيره، ثم في كون الدلالة على اختصاص الولد بالوالد من الإشارة نظر فإن اللام موضوع للاختصاص، وقد أريد ههنا الاختصاص الخاص، فالمراد بالمولود له من انتسب إليه الولد وهذا المعنى هو المقصود وإن كان القصد إليه لإيجاب النفقة عليه، فالدلالة عليه عبارة لا إشارة نعم الدلالة على ترتب الأحكام المذكورة على ثبوت النسب إشارة البتة فافهم (وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ الَّذِينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَارِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ۸] الآية فإنه وإن سيق لإيجاب سهم الغنيمة لهم (دل على زوال الملك عما خلفوا لأن الفقير من لا يملك شيئاً من المال، ففي التعبير عنهم بالفقير إشارة إلى زوال الملك، وإلا صاروا أغنياء (لا يقال لفظ الفقير (استعارة لإضافة الأموال إليهم) فيكونون ملاك الأموال، فلا يكونون فقراء ، بل استعير لمن انقطع طمعه عن الانتفاع بالمال لأن الإضافة الدالة على الملك حين (الإخراج من الديار والأموال (لا تنافي الفقر (الآن) فلا تصلح الإضافة قرينة على ثبوت الاستعارة فيترك الفقير على الحقيقة (و) قال (في «التحرير» : والوجه أنه أي زوال الملك بل الدلالة عليه (اقتضاء لأن صحة إطلاق الفقير بعد ثبوت ملك) الفقير الأموال) متوقفة على الزوال فيكون الزوال لازماً متقدماً والدلالة عليه اقتضاء (أقول) إطلاق الفقراء وإن توقف على زوال الملك، لكن لا يتوقف على الزوال بالاستيلاء، فكون الاستيلاء مزيلا) ملك المؤمنين (موجباً للملك لهم أي للمستولين الكفار (ثابت بالإشارة عن كما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: ﴿أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَرِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ ﴾ [الحشر: ٨] لأن التعليق بالمشتق يوجب عليه المبدأ فالإخراج سبب الفقر فتدبر) وهذا غير وافٍ فإن كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً وموجباً حكم، ونفس زوال الملك حكم آخر، وصاحب التحرير إنما حكم على الثاني بكونه اقتضاء دون الأوّل فتدبر ؛ فالأولى في الجواب ما قاله مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره إن توقف الإطلاق على أمر لا يوجب كونه اقتضاء ، وإلا لزم أن يكون جميع اللوازم اقتضاء لتوقف الإطلاق عليها البتة بل الاقتضاء الدلالة على أمر يتوقف عليه صحة المعنى المفهوم، وليس ههنا كذلك فإن زوال الملك والفقر معان من غير توقف لأحدهما على الآخر فلم تكن إلا إشارة هذا وبعد بقي في الكلام كلام فإنه يدل الفقير مطابقة على من لا يملك شيئاً، فكون المهاجرين رضوان الله تعالى عليهم غير مالكي ما خلفوا مقصوده في الجملة، وإن لم يكن مقصوداً بالذات فهو عبارة ؛ نعم الدلالة على كون الاستيلاء مزيلاً موجباً غير مقصود إشارة فافهم (وكقوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ هُنَّ لِبَاسٌ لَكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ لِبَاسٌ لَّهُنَّ عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَعَفَا عَنكُمْ فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ وَابْتَغُوا مَا كَتَبَ اللهُ لَكُمْ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى الَّيْلِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] (دل) هذا القول على جواز الإصباح جنباً) للصائم، لا كما يقوله الروافض خذلهم الله تعالى : من أصبح جنباً فقد أفطر وتقريره على ما هو المشهور أن الغاية دلت على جواز الاستمتاع بهنّ إلى الفجر فجاز الاستمتاع في آخر أجزاء الليل، وهو يستلزم كونه جنباً في أول أجزاء الفجر، وأورد عليه أن حتى غاية للأكل والشرب، فيجوزان في آخر أجزاء الليل لا الاستمتاع بالنساء، وأجيب بأن حتى غاية لقوله: ﴿فَالْآنَ بَاشِرُوهُنَّ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] إلى الآخر بدلالة السياق، فإن الآية في نفي حرمة الاستمتاع والأكل والشرب، من بعد ثلث الليل، فأبيح الأشياء الثلاثة إلى الفجر، ولو سلمنا وتنزلنا فالاستمتاع مثل الأكل والشرب، فإذا جازا إلى آخر الليل جاز أيضاً بمفهومه الموافق، لكن على هذا كونه من باب الإشارة غير ظاهر، وسلك المصنف مسلكاً آخر هو أن قوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] دل بعبارته على حل الاستمتاع بهن في الليل كله فلزم الإصباح جنباً (فإنه لازم من استغراق الليل بالرفث قطعاً) وعلى هذا لا شائبة للإيراد عليه أصلاً (قيل : اللازم) الآية (جواز الوقاع في جزء منه لا في جميعه) فإن ليلة الرفث مطلقة (أقول: قد في للاستيعاب فدل الآية على استغراق حل الرفث بالليل على أنه نسخ للحظر، المتعلق بالجميع كما روى أبو داود والبيهقي عن ابن عباس في : ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۳] قال : فكان الناس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم إذا صلوا العتمة حرم عليهم الطعام والشراب والنساء وصاموا إلى القابلة فاختان رجل نفسه فجامع امرأته وقد صلّى العشاء ولم يفطر، فأراد الله أن يجعل ذلك يسراً لمن بقي ورخصة ومنفعة فقال : ﴿عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] الآية فرخص لهم ويسر وفي رواية البخاري وأبي داود والترمذي عن البراء بن عازب قال : كان أصحاب النبي إذا كان الرجل صائماً فحضر الإفطار فنام قبل أن يفطر لم يأكل ليلته ولا يومه حتى يمسي، وأن قيس بن صرمة الأنصاري كان صائماً، وكان يومه يعمل في أرضه، فلما حضر الإفطار أتى امرأته فقال : هل عندك طعام؟ قالت : لا ولكن أنطلق فأطلب لك، فغلبته عينه فنام وجاءته امرأته فلما رأته نائماً قالت : خيبة لك أنمت فلما انتصف النهار غشي عليه فذكر ذلك للنبي فأنزلت هذه الآية أحل لكم ليلة الصيام الرفث إلى قوله : من الفجر، ففرحوا بها فرحاً شديداً وفي الروايتين نحو من التعارض، ولفظ الآية يؤيد الأولى، وعلى كل تقدير فالآية ناسخة للتحريم المستغرق جميع الليلة (فيجوز) في جميع الليل (كما كان محرماً فيها، لأن ارتفاع الحظر يلزمه الإباحة إلى أن يقوم الدليل على التحريم وليس فافهم، ثم لو تنزلنا وسلمنا أن ليلة الصيام مطلقة لم يضرنا فإنه حينئذ يدل على جواز المس في كل جزء من أجزاء الليل ومنه الأخير فلزم جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً فافهم، واعلم أن جواز إصباح الصائم جنباً ثابت بدلائل لا شبهة فيه منها ما أخرج الشيخان ومالك وابن أبي
[The passage discusses types of indication (dalalah). It begins:] It may be hidden, so its indication is hidden, and it may be theoretical due to the hiddenness of the implication. Like His statement, Exalted is He: {And upon the father [of the child] is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable} (2:233) — this verse is for obligating maintenance upon fathers, but He, Glorified, expressed them as 'the one to whom the child is born', and attributed the child to them with the letter lam, so in it there is an indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father in lineage, since possession is definitely not intended. So he alone is liable for his maintenance, and nothing is obligatory upon the mother. And this entails for this child the eligibility for the greater imamate, which is general sovereignty, so he deserves it if the father is Qurayshi, and [entails] compatibility (kafa'ah), so he becomes compatible for one whose father is compatible for him, except for freedom and slavery, for he is not free and suspended by the father's freedom or slavery, by a specific proof for both, and other related rulings like reason and others. Then, regarding the indication of the exclusivity of the child to the father being from isharah (implication), there is consideration, for the lam is placed for exclusivity, and here the specific exclusivity is intended. So what is meant by 'the one to whom the child is born' is one to whom the child is attributed, and this meaning is the intended one, even if the purpose towards it is for obligating maintenance upon him. So the indication upon it is ibarah (explicit expression), not isharah. Yes, the indication of the arrangement of the mentioned rulings upon the establishment of lineage is definitely isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties} (59:8) — although it was put forward to obligate the share of war booty for them, it indicates the removal of ownership over what they left behind, because the poor person is one who does not possess any wealth. So in describing them as poor, there is an indication of removal of ownership; otherwise they would become rich. It cannot be said that the word 'poor' is a metaphor due to the addition of wealth to them, so they would be owners of wealth and thus not poor. Rather, it is used metaphorically for one whose hope for benefiting from wealth is cut off, because the addition indicating ownership at the time of expulsion from homes and properties does not negate poverty now, so the addition does not serve as evidence for the establishment of metaphor, so 'poor' is left on its literal meaning. And the author of al-Tahrir said: The correct view is that it, i.e., the removal of ownership, or rather the indication upon it, is iqtida' (necessary implication), because the validity of applying 'poor' after the establishment of ownership of wealth is dependent on removal, so removal is necessary and prior, and the indication upon it is iqtida'. I say: The application of 'poor' although dependent on removal of ownership, is not dependent on removal by usurpation. So that usurpation is a remove of the ownership of the believers and a cause of ownership for them, i.e., for the disbeliever usurpers, is established by isharah, just as His statement points to it: {expelled from their homes and their properties} because attribution by the derived term necessitates the basis, so expulsion is the cause of poverty, so ponder. But this is insufficient, for that usurpation is a remover and a cause is a ruling, and the very removal of ownership is another ruling. The author of al-Tahrir only ruled on the second as being iqtida', not the first, so ponder. So the best answer is what the revealer of divine secrets, may Allah sanctify his secret, said: That the dependence of the application on something does not necessitate it being iqtida', otherwise all necessary concomitants would be iqtida' due to the application's absolute dependence on them. Rather, iqtida' is the indication of something on which the correctness of the understood meaning depends. And it is not like that here, for removal of ownership and poverty are meanings with no dependence of one on the other, so it was nothing but isharah. After this, there remains discussion in the speech, for 'poor' literally indicates one who possesses nothing. So that the emigrants, may Allah be pleased with them, are not owners of what they left behind is intended in general, and if not intended per se, it is ibarah. Yes, the indication that usurpation is a remover and a cause is unintended isharah, so understand. And like His statement, Exalted is He: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women. They are garments for you and you are garments for them. Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves, so He relented towards you and pardoned you. So now have relations with them and seek what Allah has written for you, and eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn. Then complete the fast until the night} (2:187). This verse indicates the permissibility of becoming junub (in a state of major ritual impurity) at dawn for the fasting person, not as the rejected Rafidah say: 'Whoever becomes junub at dawn has broken his fast.' The explanation, according to what is well-known, is that the limit (ghayah) indicated the permissibility of enjoying them until dawn, so enjoyment is permissible in the last parts of the night, which entails being junub in the first parts of dawn. An objection was raised that 'until' is a limit for eating and drinking, so they are permissible in the last parts of the night, not the enjoyment of women. The answer is that 'until' is a limit for His statement {so now have relations with them} to the end, by implication of context, for the verse is about negating the prohibition of enjoyment, eating, and drinking after one third of the night, so the three things were permitted until dawn. Even if we concede and assume, enjoyment is like eating and drinking, so if they are permissible until the end of the night, it is also permissible by its parallel meaning (mafhum muwafaqah). But on this, its being from the category of isharah is not apparent. The author took another path: that His statement {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations with your women} explicitly indicates the permissibility of enjoying them throughout the whole night, so becoming junub at dawn is necessary, for it is a necessary consequence of spending the whole night in relations. And on this, there is no trace of objection at all. It was said: What is necessitated by the verse is the permissibility of intercourse in a part of it, not all of it, for 'the night of relations' is unrestricted. I say: The letter 'lam' in 'li-laylati' is for istighraq (comprehensiveness), so the verse indicates the permissibility of relations throughout the night, and it abrogated the prohibition that pertained to the whole night, as narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas regarding {O you who believe, fasting is prescribed for you...} (2:183). He said: People at the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family, when they prayed the night prayer, food, drink, and women became forbidden to them, and they fasted until the next night. So a man betrayed himself and had intercourse with his wife after having prayed the night prayer and not broken his fast. Allah wanted to make that easy for those who remained, a concession and benefit, so He said: {Allah knew that you were betraying yourselves...} and the verse, so He granted them concession and made things easy. In another narration by al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: The Companions of the Prophet, when a man was fasting and the time of breaking fast came, if he slept before breaking fast, he would not eat that night nor the next day until evening. And Qays ibn Sirmah al-Ansari was fasting, and he was working in his land that day. When the time of breaking fast came, he went to his wife and said: Do you have food? She said: No, but I will go and seek for you. So sleep overcame him and he slept. His wife came and when she saw him sleeping, she said: Disappointment for you! You slept. When midday came, he lost consciousness. That was mentioned to the Prophet, so this verse was revealed: {It is made lawful for you on the night of fasting to have relations...} up to His saying 'from the dawn'. They rejoiced greatly at it. The two narrations are somewhat contradictory, and the wording of the verse supports the first. In any case, the verse abrogates the prohibition that covered the entire night, so it is permissible throughout the whole night, just as it was prohibited in it, because the removal of prohibition necessitates permissibility until evidence for prohibition comes, and there is none, so understand. Then even if we concede and accept that 'the night of fasting' is unrestricted, it does not harm us, for then it indicates the permissibility of intercourse in every part of the night, including the last, so the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is necessitated, so understand. And know that the permissibility of the fasting person becoming junub at dawn is established by proofs with no doubt, including what al-Bukhari, Muslim, Malik, and Ibn Abi...
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the various types of textual indication (dalalah) in Quranic verses, specifically focusing on 'dalalat al-isharah' (indication by implication) as opposed to 'dalalat al-ibarah' (explicit indication). The author, commenting on 'Muslim al-Thubut', uses three examples to illustrate how verses can imply rulings beyond their immediate explicit meaning. 

The first example is Quran 2:233 concerning maintenance of children. The verse explicitly obligates the father to provide for his child's mother, but through the phrase 'al-mawludu lahu' (the one to whom the child is born) and the use of the possessive 'lam', it implies the exclusive lineage of the child to the father. The author then explains that this exclusivity is actually a clear expression (ibarah) of lineage, not merely an implication (isharah). However, the subsequent rulings—such as eligibility for imamate, compatibility in marriage, and other legal consequences—are indeed derived through isharah from the establishment of lineage. This nuanced distinction shows the careful application of usul terminology.

The second example is Quran 59:8 referring to the poor emigrants. The verse is primarily for allocating the spoils to them, but describing them as 'poor' implies that they lost ownership of the property they left behind. The author discusses an objection that 'poor' might be metaphorical, since they still had ownership at the time of expulsion. The response clarifies that the description is literal because ownership was removed, and the indication of removal is isharah. The author then engages with the view of 'al-Tahrir' that this is iqtida' (necessary implication) and refines the analysis, concluding that it is isharah.

The third and most extensive example is Quran 2:187, which permits marital relations during Ramadan nights. This verse implicitly indicates that a fasting person may be in a state of janabah (major impurity) at dawn, contrary to the Rafidah view. The author presents several arguments: (1) The limit (ghayah) 'until dawn' applies to all permitted activities—eating, drinking, and relations—so engaging in relations in the last part of the night leads to janabah at dawn. (2) Even if 'until' only applies to eating and drinking, the same permissibility for relations is derived by qiyas or mafhum muwafaqah. (3) The author's preferred argument is that the verse literally permits relations throughout the whole night (istighraq), so janabah at dawn is a necessary consequence. He supports this with narrations about the abrogation of a prior stricter rule that prohibited any activity after evening prayer. The passage concludes by asserting that the permissibility is well-established with clear proofs.

Key Terms
الغاية (al-ghāyah): Limit or endpoint: the term 'hatta' (until) which sets a temporal boundary.
الرفث (al-rafath): Sexual intercourse or intimate relations; in the Quranic context, referring to marital relations during fasting nights.
دلالة الإشارة (dalālat al-ishārah): Indication by implication: where the text implies a meaning that is not the primary intended meaning but follows from it necessarily or by context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis of Quran 2:187, why does the permissibility of janabah at dawn for a fasting person qualify as dalalat al-isharah?
A) Because it is explicitly stated in the verse.
B) Because it is a necessary consequence of the permission of relations until dawn.
C) Because it is derived from the practice of the Companions alone.
D) Because it is an exception to the general rule.

Key Takeaway
From Quran 2:187, the Hanafi school derives that a fasting person's fast is valid even if they are junub at dawn, using dalalat al-isharah based on the permission of relations throughout the night.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
Refuting Arguments from Companion Statements and Quranic Apparent Meaning
Hanafi refutation of twin usul objections to conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi usul position that a Companion's statement and a Quranic verse's apparent meaning are not decisive against istihsan and established practice.

Core Idea
A Companion's statement and a Quranic verse's literal wording may not defeat established practice and istihsan.

In this passage, the Hanafi school responds to two objections against the validity of conditional divorce pronounced before marriage. The first objection invokes a report from Ali that such a divorce is 'nothing'. The second cites the apparent meaning of Quran 33:49, which mentions divorce after marriage. The Hanafi response demonstrates how a Companion's statement can be outweighed by other reports and how a verse's scope can be limited by interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first objection and its evidence
The opponent cites a report from Ali (via al-Hasan al-Basri) that a conditional divorce before marriage is invalid. Note the chain and how the opponent uses it as proof.
The report is from Abd al-Razzaq; the opponent argues that the absence of meeting between al-Hasan and Ali weakens it, but the Hanafi side counters that the chains are mutawatir.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to the first objection
The Hanafi response offers two lines: (a) the report is contradicted by other reports (e.g., from Qasim ibn Muhammad, with Umar's practice) that show such conditions are valid; (b) the attack on the chain is invalid—the narrators are trustworthy and the chains reach tawatur.
Note the use of contradiction (mu'arada) and the rejection of negative evidence.
3
Identify the second objection and its evidence
The opponent cites Quran 33:49, which says 'when you marry... then divorce', implying that divorce only occurs after marriage. Ibn Abbas interpreted this to exclude divorce before marriage.
The opponent uses the apparent meaning (zahir) of the verse.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the second objection
The Hanafi response argues that the verse only gives a ruling for divorce after marriage (before consummation); it does not address or negate the validity of a conditional divorce pronounced before marriage. Ibn Abbas's interpretation is not binding because the wording does not support it (la yatahammalu al-lafz).
Key point: the verse is not 'amm covering all types of divorce; it is specific to a scenario.
5
Synthesize the outcome and thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the Hanafi ruling that a conditional divorce before marriage is valid upon marriage stands, supported by istihsan and practice of other Companions, overriding the objections.
This illustrates how a Companion's statement (qawl al-sahabi) and a Quranic zahir can be overridden by stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا رابعاً: روى عبد الرزاق عن أمير المؤمنين علي كرم الله وجهه، قال الحسن البصري : سأل رجل علياً قال : قلت : إن تزوّجت فلانة فهي طالق فقال علي: ليس بشيء، وهذا إنما يتمشى منهم بطريق الجدل، وإلا فقول الصحابي ليس حجة عندهم، قلنا: معارض مالك بما روى في الموطأ) أن سعيد بن عمر بن سليم الرازقي سأل قاسم بن محمد عن رجل طلق امرأته إن هو تزوّجها، فقال القاسم إن رجلاً جعل امرأته كظهر أمه إن هو تزوّجها، فأمره ه عمر إن هو تزوّجها لا يقربها حتى يكفر كفارة المظاهر، كذا في «فتح القدير»، وأما يصح الجواب بأن أهل الحديث قالوا : لم يلاق الحسن أمير المؤمنين علياً كرم الله فلا وجهه، الاحتجاج به فليس بشيء، فإنهم شهداء على النفي، وقد اتفقوا على كونهما في المدينة مدة، فعدم اللقاء بعيد، ثم أصحاب السلاسل قاطبة نقلوا السند متصلاً، لا ريبة في اتصاله وملاقاته، والطعن فيهم لا يجترىء عليه مسلم ويضحك من عقله الصبيان وأيضاً قد بلغ الأسانيد حد التواتر والرواة كلهم أولياء أصحاب كرامات وبالجملة : الشك فيه زلة عظيمة فافهم، وأما رد الجواب بأن المرسل ليس حجة فليس بوارد إذ مقصوده أنه ليس حجة عند معارضة المسند، وما عن أمير المؤمنين عمر مسند هذا، وقالوا خامساً : قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَايُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا نَكَحْتُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ ثُمَّ طَلَقْتُمُوهُنَّ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٩] روى عبد الرزاق عن ابن جريج قال: بلغ ابن عباس أن ابن مسعود يقول : إن طلق ما لم ينكح فهو جائز، قال ابن عباس، أخطأ في هذا، إن الله يقول : إِذَا نَكَحْتُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ ثُمَّ طَلَّقْتُمُوهُنَّ مِن قَبْلِ أَن تَمَسُّوهُنَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٩] ولم يقل : إذا طلقتم المؤمنات ثم نكحتموهن قلنا ليس في الآية نفي عدم صحة التعليق بالملك، بل فيه حكم ما إذا نكح ثم طلق قبل المس وتأويل ابن عباس لا يقبل لعدم تحمل اللفظ، ولمعارضة
And they said fourthly: 'Abd ar-Razzaq narrated from the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali (may Allah honor his face): al-Hasan al-Basri said: A man asked 'Ali: I said, 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' 'Ali said: 'It is nothing.' This is only maintained by them through argumentation; otherwise, the saying of a Companion is not a proof according to them. We said: it is contradicted by what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta': that Sa'id ibn 'Umar ibn Sulaym ar-Raziqi asked al-Qasim ibn Muhammad about a man who divorced his wife if he were to marry her. Al-Qasim said: A man made his wife like the back of his mother if he were to marry her, and 'Umar ordered him, if he were to marry her, not to approach her until he expiates the expiation of zihar. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. As for the claim that the people of hadith said that al-Hasan did not meet the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali, so there is no authority for using it as proof, this is nothing. For they are witnesses to a negative, and they agreed that both were in Medina for a period, so the absence of meeting is unlikely. Moreover, the chains of transmission have been transmitted as connected (muttasil) by all authorities without doubt, and a Muslim does not dare to impugn them; even children would laugh at the intellect of anyone who does. Additionally, the chains have reached the level of tawatur, and all the narrators are awliya' and people of miracles. In short, doubt in this is a great slip, so understand. As for the rejection that a mursal is not proof, it is not valid because his point is that it is not proof when opposing a musnad; what is from the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar is musnad. And they said fifthly: Allah Almighty said: {O you who believe, when you marry believing women and then divorce them...} [al-Ahzab: 49]. 'Abd ar-Razzaq narrated from Ibn Jurayj: It reached Ibn 'Abbas that Ibn Mas'ud said: If he divorces what he has not married, it is permissible. Ibn 'Abbas said: He erred in this. Allah says: {When you marry believing women and then divorce them before you have touched them} and He did not say: 'When you divorce believing women and then marry them.' We said: There is no negation in the verse of the validity of suspension (ta'liq) on ownership; rather, it contains the ruling of when one marries and then divorces before touching. Ibn 'Abbas's interpretation is not acceptable because the wording does not bear it, and due to contradiction.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage addresses two remaining objections. The fourth objection cites a report from 'Ali (RA) that a conditional divorce before marriage is 'nothing'. The Hanafi response: this report is contradicted by other reports (e.g., from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad transmitted by Malik in al-Muwatta') that show the validity of such a condition. They also refute the claim that al-Hasan al-Basri did not meet 'Ali, arguing that the chains are authentic and the meeting is established. The fifth objection quotes the Quranic verse (al-Ahzab 33:49) which orders divorce after marriage, implying that divorce before marriage is invalid. The Hanafi response: the verse deals with the ruling for divorce after marriage before consummation, not with the validity of conditional divorce before marriage. It does not negate the possibility of suspending divorce on a future marriage. The interpretation of Ibn 'Abbas is not binding because the wording does not support it, and it is contradicted.

Key Terms
قول الصحابي (qawl al-sahabi): The statement of a Companion, used as a source in some arguments.
التأويل (al-ta'wil): Interpretation of a text beyond its apparent meaning.
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Contradiction between two evidence sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why is the Quranic verse (33:49) not a proof against conditional divorce?
A) The verse is abrogated
B) It only regulates divorce after marriage, not before
C) It applies only to immediate divorce
D) The verse is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
A Companion's statement and a Quranic verse's apparent meaning can be overridden by stronger evidence, such as contradictory reports and context-based interpretation.
